O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the final in the study of medicine together with its fulfillment, and I have made an end through its explanations and by its demonstrations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and foreign to all, so it's lost its knowledge and been cut off; only small descriptions remain in books from ancient times, by those whose hands have moved them.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come errors and vanity, intentions have been closed off and knowledge has been kept away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I will revive it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of iron instruments for cauterization, and other surgical tools along with their preparation as required.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine has become elongated.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who undertakes this must surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and the number of them, and their movement and moving veins and resting ones, and where they exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates says that knowledge without action is useless, and it is only with practice that one excels; especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that one who is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things should be careful not to fall into error and cause harm to others; as I have often seen many of those who venture into this field without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut into an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck and severed the arteries there; so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a bladder stone in a man with hot oil, and the stone was large; he carried away with it a part of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and indeed if they cut it out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who took care of the Duke of our land, who had a broken leg with an open wound; and due to their ignorance, the surgeons set the break over the wound using strong ligatures, leaving no room for drainage, and left it like that for some time; they instructed him not to remove it; and as a result, his leg swelled up completely, his foot became infected, and he was lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come and release his leg; and when I undid the ligatures, he felt peace and no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But nevertheless, the corruption was already established in the member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And then I saw another physician who would open an abscess, and it would then become inflamed due to the evil nature of his work.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a cancerous sore, when it is purged of melancholic humour, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all the corrupt matter can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, my dear son, it is necessary that you know that surgical work is divided into two categories: one where there is danger in several cases; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you. Take up your arms in confidence, approach your patients gently yet firmly, and employ the better method so that by God's grace, you may come to a successful outcome and gain praise; leave behind those terrifying diseases with great sanctity; remove your armor from what makes you doubt yourself, and have faith in yourself, so that you can pass from this world to the other in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on any severe illness as a patient unless you want to be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and other medical treatments that use heat, and this chapter is arranged from the head down to the feet; it describes the forms of instruments, the tools for cauterization, and everything else necessary for the procedure.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping, wounds, arrow extractions, and similar matters; the chapter orders and describes the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters; it is ordered from the head to the feet, and describes the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Now that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to speak of the quality of help and harm in each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest speech, subtlest science, and greatest secret; many wise men spoke about this and agreed upon it; their words are sufficient for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization universally aids all constitutions where there is matter involved, except for two constitutions: hot constitution without matter and dry constitution without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the combination of hot and dry constitution with matter, some argued that cauterization is greatly beneficial while others said the opposite: that it is not useful for illnesses caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, it should not be used to treat illnesses caused by heat or dryness, and those who say otherwise claim that cauterization greatly aids in treating hot and dry diseases within the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the male body and its moisture to the constitution of fire, you find the former cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, only someone who has tried it and understands through long practice the chapter on cauterization, the diversity of human constitutions, their dispositions and causes of illness, their progressions, and according to time; we are not afraid of other constitutions, especially with regards to cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors agreed and consented to cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of healing and has greater benefit than any burning medicinal herb.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come forth except to the member that is cooked, and it harms no other member if left unchecked.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines pass from member to another in aloignant, and cause the member long-lasting illness; and by chance they kill the patient fire due to its height and the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is no superfluidity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and the length of my service and study in the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this I apologize for the length of speech, as I do not wish to take away the secret that is hidden in fire, and the quality of its work, how it removes illness from bodies, just as the philosopher says in demonstration; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be performed, and they chose a suitable time for it.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that cauterization is suitable at any time, for the harm that may arise can be mitigated by its aid; especially if the cauterizations are necessary and urgent due to severe pain, where waiting could lead to greater damage to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, my dear son, like the foolish surgeon does; for the illness that is healed by cauterization will not return; and they say it so; but it is not as they believe, because cauterization is only a medicine that alters the complexion, dries up the humors causing pain, and is better than medication due to its swift action, and the power of its effect.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; 
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauterization is valuable after medical treatments, their understanding is false, and cauterization is indeed the final step in medicine because when we apply various treatment methods for any illness and they are ineffective, then we perform cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is apparent that cauterization is the last resort in medicine, not according to the misguided beliefs of ignorant doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancient masters said that cauterization with a golden instrument is more beneficial than with iron, and they attributed this to the quality of gold and the superiority of its material; and they claimed that the color of the cauterized wound does not cause harm, but I have proven this false as it is true for some patients; and gold cautery is indeed more effective than iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat the golden instrument, you cannot know when it is hot due to the color of gold, and it cools down quickly; if heated too much, they burn in the fire; thus there are enough obstacles here.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use the iron cautery which we have specially adapted for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Here I have ordered this chapter from head to foot so that the path is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive-oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness in the brain, and it can be done because of a disease called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head into the eyes, ears, for multiple dreams and toothaches and sore throat, and especially all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by solvent medicine over three or four nights, according to their health and constitution as well as what they can tolerate; and then have the head shaved.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make them sit cross-legged in your hands, and place their hands on top of yours; after that put the root of your palm on the root of their nose between both eyes; let your two means come together, so bleed with this then heat up the cautery which is called 'olivare', of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on an inky spot, and do this by moving your hand down and squeezing it back and forth repeatedly; then lift your hand slightly, and reapply the cautery to the place until you see bone if you don't see any yet as I told you before; after take a pouch of fine silk, and put moist cotton inside, and place on the spot, leaving it there for three days; afterwards put some butter-soaked cotton on top; and leave it in place until the burning sensation is gone; then treat the wound with an ointment called 'tetrafarmacon', until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if the elders say that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; thus, aiding its healing process.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one must let the cauterization burn until a part of the bone is charred, and then restore what has been burned from the bone, to be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one must keep the cauterization going until it penetrates deeply, pushing so hard that bone is also scraped away to the width of a woman's hairpin because this allows the humors to exit more readily; and they say you should let the wound remain open for some time afterwards; then you must clean it and seal it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And I do not think either of these methods of cauterization to be good at all in every case, except perhaps where there is fear; and it seems to me that I should leave this alone; for the shoulder joint becomes weakened by continuous discharge due to natural causes, as we have witnessed elsewhere in other limbs; likewise when a patient's shoulder joint is weak by nature, and the first method of cauterization appears safer and more beneficial to me, so I use it thus in practice.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from old head pain
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the head there is chronic pain that persists for a long time, the patient must use herbs and pills called 'cochie', and purgatives for the head, oils, and plasters; and if one performs the cauterization we mentioned before, but it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be cautious if the patient's shoulder is of strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterize below that cautery we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, make a cauterization on each corner of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and do it where there is a place called 'vessel'; these are places where one applies cups; and lighten your hand so you do not reach the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak about it later; and make sure that the cauteries of the corners are subtler than those used on the middle part of the head, and here is how.
dou cautere dou chief	For the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in a part of the head and extends up to the eye, and the head has been cleansed with purgative medicines, and other treatments I have mentioned for diseases have been applied without success; then cauterization is performed in two ways: with hot dry medicine or with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with hot dry medicine is done as follows: take a piece of aloes wood and remove the bark, then cut it into two halves, and make an incision in the temple where the pain is located so that you can place the aloes beneath the skin; once placed there, bind and hold it firmly for twelve hours; after this time, untie it and treat with strong garlic juice, leaving the wound as is for two or three days; then apply a cotton swab soaked in butter until healing occurs.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment, wait until it is healed; and if you wish to do so, make use of certain burning medications that I have described in the twelfth chapter about burning medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner:
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, which has this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called a 'clos' because the tip is made in the shape of a bell with a little curve and has a small opening at its center; place it on the painful spot, keep your hand steady, and turn the iron slightly so that half of the pointed edge is heated; lift your hand before the artery burns, which is outside, and a lot of blood will flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After apply cotton in aw of silk, and place it on the site for three days; then add moistened cotton with butter, and finally clean the wound of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with a 'cultellare' cautery, at all its point, take care not to cut the artery in this fresh migraine.
de emigraine	Of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a migraine as we mentioned before in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the previous cauterization methods with medicine and iron do not suffice, then you must heat the 'cultellare' cautery until it is white; incise over the site drawing a line half an inch long, remove your hand once, and be careful not to cut the artery or reach the bone; beware of the mandible's movement while chewing, ensure that no muscle spasm occurs in the patient, and watch out for arterial bleeding when it is cut, as this has great risk especially for those who are unaware, unstudied, and inexperienced; leave the operation halfway. But I will tell you how to staunch blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you where this is explained in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these caustics are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, apply the cautery which we mentioned in the chapter on extracting an artery, with a cautery that has two knives; and this cautery is better than the former one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From earache due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When earache occurs due to coldness and one has applied solvent medicines and other treatments as we have mentioned in the classification, but pain does not subside, then heat this cautery which is called a "point":
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pricking all around the affected ear, or both if pain persists in both ears, and move a little above the root of the ear when you have marked the spot to cauterize; make ten points around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated by cauterization is only for those that come from flux, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not apply cautery to those that arise from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torture that comes from a flux of eels and purgations of the head, and gargling, and it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and the third at the join of the two lips; place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and burn towards the head of the ear just above the corner of the forehead, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; leave the cautery in place until half of the heart's beat has passed; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the small knife we mentioned before, but it is a little more delicate and the blade should be slightly thicker; after treating the wound as I said earlier, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is an old condition and you treat it as we have said earlier, but the patient does not improve and has no fever, then make four cauterizations: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the place called 'vassal', as we mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; treat them as we have said earlier.
de litargie	Of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large doses of lead oxide and pills that purify the brain; then wash his head thoroughly, and apply a mustard plaster to the back of the head according to what is written in the treatise on plasters; and here is how you perform cauterization: do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, apply three fire cauteries within the head descending to the neck, with a space of two finger-widths between each cautery; treat them as you would others, and if you wish to combine them, and the patient can tolerate it, make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, add two more on the two corners, treating until healed; these cauteries are called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleaned of hairs and as previously mentioned; afterwards, comb the patient's head, then apply a fire cautery in the middle of the head and on each corner, one at the back, and three along the spine of the neck; if more is required, and their body is moist and they can tolerate it, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries along the spine of the back; let it burn until the strongest part of the heart is affected, then lift your hand away; treat them until healed, and these cauteries are called "olivare" as previously stated.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not undergo fire cauterization unless they are phlegmatic; first, the brain must be cleansed with herbs and other treatments as we have described in the division for when the patient is large and suffers from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot withstand this, let him gargle and chew, cleansing the brain often with good meat; afterwards, seize his head in the middle, and perform the cauterization as we have said before, cauterizing the vessel and each corner; and if the patient is strong and suffers, perform cauterizations as I have described for one who has paralysis and bodily weakness, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterization be olive-oil based as I have stated.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform this subtle cauterization procedure as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause of melancholy is due to excess or corrupted moisture and thick phlegm, then cauterize with several cauterizations as we have mentioned for those suffering from paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause of melancholy is due to an excess declining into melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will cleanse their brain, as mentioned previously in the classification.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, clean the patient's head; then make a well-formed linen bandage, like a circle, and place it on their head; have the patient sit with crossed legs, holding still from all sides; apply the liniment, preferably made of old sheep butter; heat it to a moderate fire so that when applied to the head, they can tolerate it; after emptying the circle within the head, let it cool down; perform this procedure once a week on the patient along with other good treatments until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you wish to cauterize with fire, make several small points across the entire cautery area.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery moistens the brain greatly; then apply cotton moistened with butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' pain
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When pain first arises in the eyes due to the symptoms I mentioned earlier, then begin by giving the patient something that purifies the head and protects it from moisture, and make them sweat in a bath multiple times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After, instruct them to bow their head and cauterize between the temples, performing two cauteries if the pain descends into both eyes simultaneously or one if it is in just one; cauterize all veins and arteries that are beneath the heart, making the cautery long according to the width of the temple; be careful of excessive bleeding and should you see too much blood flow, stop the bleeding as best you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and the caution during incision, how to staunch it; sometimes a cautery or ligature is made below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are over the veins, or near the arteries that appear outside the head; and it is seen to be from cold phlegmatic superfluities, then make the cautery as I said at the beginning descending towards the eyes: one cautery between the brows, two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or ligatures below the two bones; if more is needed, cautiously cauterize above the eyebrow with very small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	From the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit, then give the patient to drink three nights of cock's blood; afterwards, raise his head, and cauterize him in the middle over the olive [bone]; and make two 'clavilis' cauteries above the two wrists, a little below the hairline; and beware of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called 'clavilis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper [cornea] of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called 'olive'.
de coi ci est li forme:	From which this happens:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that do two cauterizations on the two eyebrows as long as the eyelashes are; and leave it be until the third part of the paper is burnt, according to the way I said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	Of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes turn inwards and prick the eye, and a cauterization is made in two ways: either with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then place the patient in your care; afterwards, draw on the paper of the eyes a shape that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be by the hairs; then put moist cotton with egg white and parsley poultice on the eye, then heat the cautery for which here is its form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the marked figure little by little many times until the heart of the sign is burned there; and the signs of a successful operation are that you see the paper retracting, and the hairs rising at the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it so for three days, afterwards put moist cotton with butter as long as the scald remains; after treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterward the hairs grow and the flesh is softened again, then resume the cautery on that same spot as you did before; and if the hair has fallen out, cauterize it until the skin rises to its natural place, and becomes even, not pricking the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and evenly, then take parchment and make a shape like a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and live coals, one third each, and grind them together well; do it quickly so it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you made like the myrtle leaf, and put it on the paper over the eye(s); if the patient's trouble is in one eye alone, operate with one; but for both eyes likewise; place under each eye cotton moistened with egg white; let the patient's head be in your lap, and place your finger pointing at the medicine, pressing one paw and the snout every time the patient feels a stinging sensation from the medicine, since they feel it as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the bite has passed, lift up the skin, and observe whether you see the paper raised just as it was previously lifted by fire or by incision; if so, then all is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply more medicine to the place where it was previously opened, until your work is even and your eyes are sharp; then cover with cotton moistened in butter until the burnt flesh falls away, after cure the place of treatment which is called "diaphenes" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must be careful in your work, take great care that none of the medicine goes into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft later on, and hairs grow in the eye, start the medicine treatment again on that softened area of the paper specifically, just as you did before; after healing is complete; this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men vary in size and smallness, and according to this, adjust your methods; do not abandon the right path for one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula with cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not bring improvement, then it is necessary to perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head on your hand; hold the minister's head between your hands so it does not move or shift; then apply moist cotton wool in egg white or parsley juice onto the eye; afterwards heat the cautery which is shaped like a pigeon feather cap, let the cautery be with you; if you wish, point it from one end to the other, and also have it like a tent; but nevertheless, this pointed cap is best for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards press the fistula if it is open and drain the pus, then dry it; if it is closed, operate on it and force out the bowels; afterwards place a hot cautery carefully, and hold your hand over the cautery at the knuckle above the eye, so that your hand does not slip; put the cautery into the fatty tissue of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you cauterize down to the bone at the beginning, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, you restart the cautery again, and do another if needed, leaving it for three days. After that, apply cotton moistened in butter, and treat with a drying ointment until it is healed. If forty days pass without healing, use corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; then treat according to what follows in this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a method of cauterizing for fistulas that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	If you find a fistula, open the spot with a knife. After that, insert into the opening one slender camel hair of the kind used for this procedure.
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	et they make it to the quantity of a .З. of lead; and hold your hand or metal plate firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the molten lead does not flow into his eye; and one must place on the patient's eye moist cotton soaked in egg white or oil: the lead thus fills the place of the fistula, and the healthy tissue passes through with marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization we mentioned, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, one must administer the perforation with a knife, and bring the fistula back to the body of the nail according to what is appropriate in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks on lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur on lips called "scabs," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as mentioned in the previous section, and the treatment is not beneficial, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on the cracks with pressure until it reaches the bottom; afterward, clean the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	The abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the tonsil, palate, or tooth roots, it becomes infected and swollen, turning into a fistula; you treat it as mentioned earlier, but if it doesn't heal: then take a cautery according to the size of the fistula; open the fistula's hole, and keep your hand steady until the hot iron reaches its bottom and back; do this once or twice, after treating it as previously mentioned in 'Treatments', until it is healed; if it heals this way, that's good; but if not, then you must uncover the area and remove any rotten bone according to what you find in the relevant chapter.
dou movement des dens	For the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine which doesn't work, then place the patient's head on your lap; afterward heat the cautery that will be formed as follows: put a rod over the tooth; insert the hot cautery inside immediately, keeping your hand steady so the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then withdraw your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your wish; after fill the patient's mouth with salt water, let him keep it for an hour and rinse his mouth with cold water.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way the moving tooth is confirmed in place, and the softened gum is restrained, while the corrupted moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain arises due to coldness, whether it is present or imaginary, and medical treatments are ineffective, then there is a need for cautery in two ways: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is performed as follows: take cow butter and place a portion of it in an iron or brass spoon; then, wrap cotton around the tip of a toothpick and dip it in boiling butter; apply this to the aching tooth until it cools down; repeat often enough for its healing properties to reach the root of the tooth. If you wish, you can moisten wool and cotton with cold butter and place it on the painful tooth, then put a hot iron against it until the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauterization with fire is such that you take a cane of iron or copper, and it should be thick enough so the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; after heating the cautery, which will be explained later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cauterization has cooled down; do this often, for the pain will be removed that very day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the urgency of this cauterization, and then let it cool afterward; this is the method for cauterization:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And cauterize any part of the head you wish to, depending on your ability; this is the method for the cane:
des scrophules	Some scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofulas are caused by a cold and damp humour, and do not respond to digestion through medication, then heat the cautery with its chimney, from which smoke emerges afterwards, and make two openings for the smoke at the other end of the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or as many times as necessary until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, use a cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it like this for three days; then apply moist cotton with butter until the burning sensation subsides; afterward treat the area with ointments and dressings until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the chimney:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the liver channels, especially when it arises from cold constitution, then the patient must first be purged by solutive medicines; after that, cauterize at the root of the throat, and take care not to go near the throat, only burning a little bit below the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then perform another cauterization at the nape of the neck where it joins with the skull, and let the cauterizations which are called "clavicle" be done as mentioned before; treat the wound as we have said earlier until it is healed.
de la toust	From the cough.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all lung diseases are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and it is an old illness, then perform two cauterizations over the axilla in their armpits; another cauterization in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let these be the "clavicle" cauterizations as mentioned before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see fit, perform the fire cautery by pricking with the 'point' which is previously described for treating ear infections; and let there be thirty points or so around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the site according to what has been said before, let there be three rows of cautery marks in this pattern:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cauterization is more gentle when done in three rows at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder dislocation.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; 
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the ribs, and four cautery marks would appear; and for this reason, cauterization is done with a three-pronged cauterizer, thus the pattern of six cauterizations is formed; and these nerves follow the subtle path of a tent, which is the shape of the three-pronged cauterizer.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	and sometimes it is adjusted over this one nerve, so there are eight cauterizations instead.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, place the small round cauterizer on top and grind it with a needle; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it dislocates again soon after, then do a cauterization on the thick part of the collarbone, with many small cauterizations close together.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and excess moisture affect the stomach to such an extent that it is drawn away from its natural balance, and catarrh multiplies within him, and with usual treatments he does not improve, then it is necessary for the patient to be reminded of his posture on his back, and to extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Thereafter make three cauteries underneath the navel with a spoon-shaped tool of the size of a thumb, for the whole cautery is clinched, and two cauteries outside the two sides such that the shape of the cauteries be at three angles, and let there be enough space between one and another that they are not joined together when casting off scurf; and let the cautery be so perfect that it cleanses the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauterys be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Et if you want to cauterize with a large cautery on the stomach according to this method; and for those who fear this cautery, first prick and bleed at that same spot on the stomach. Mark a point according to the size you wish to cauterize; then apply the entire 'point' cautery.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the wound that we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver suffers pain from cold and moisture and large accumulations of gas, so that it is thrown out of its natural state by superfluities; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit him, then the patient must be reminded of his condition; and apply three cauteries according to this form, figure, and size on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the man's coat hangs; and leave a space between each cautery equal to the thickness of a finger; let the cauteries run lengthwise along the body, do not press down too hard with your whole hand at any point during the procedure; only burn halfway through the heart of the liver, and have the patient standing upright on their feet; if they cannot stand, then let them lie down, stretch out their legs, and raise their arms; this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your wish is to cauterize these cauteries with the lancet, if you are skilled and wise in this art, be careful not to burn the entire heart, for you would cause the whole body to dry up; and do not reach the mouth, as the heart is very delicate there, and know it well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is within the flesh of the liver or its membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient will feel a pain that is not too severe; but if it is in the membrane, they will suffer unbearable pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And so when this treatment requires it, the patient must be reminded of the care needed for their head; then bleed from a nearby spot where the abscess is located, and then heat the cautery which resembles a ray [fish], due to its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with fire until the heart is burnt, and it reaches as far as the sifac, so that the pores are all closed; afterwards treat according to the treatment of eschars until it is healed; and no one should use this cautery except those who have studied medicine for a long time, and by whose hands these diseases have sometimes been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may operate boldly, and yet it seems to me that one is better off leaving him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	scarring scarification
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleuresis one should make cauteries with the roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a root of aristolochia which is long, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, also thick and as long as your two fingers; moisten it with oil, then apply it to the fire, and cauterize with a cautery between the armpit and neck, and two small cauteries somewhat lower down on that part which is below the beard; two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly behind; one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another over the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on either side of the chest outside the cautery which is between the two shoulders; do not press your hand hard, but apply it gently as if you were smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient authorities said that any man should use fire cautery like the barber, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess, which removes pain as we have already stated for liver abscesses.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this procedure there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula may develop which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of mice as we have stated in the division of treatments, and it does not improve, then there are three types of cautery which are all beneficial.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	One way is to perform three or four cauterizations in a line following the length of the mouse, following the shape of the liver cautery as we have stated before; do not press your hand on all the cauterizations, and let the patient lie prone on their back; another way of cauterizing is to heat the two-nerved cautery as we showed in shoulder dislocation; lift up the heart which is above the mouse, or where the pain of the patient comes from the left side, and make the elevations you lift up the heart according to the heart, following the length of the body, and let the cauterizations be according to the width of the body.
