Never are found in the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, barks that are ugly and rough; sometimes these teeth become black or yellow-green and wormy, so much so that corruption reaches the gum, making them stink; have the patient sit with their head in your lap, then pull any bark where it appears, until nothing remains; do this also for the blackish, greenish, yellowish and other such discolorations, until they are cleaned; if you remove what is present due to the initial reason, that's good; if not, repeat on the second and third day, until everything has been removed; know that teeth require various instruments of different shapes to be extracted according to their condition, because the rasp used to extract teeth from above have a different form than those used in between them; these forms and others should therefore always be available.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay in extracting it as much as you can, for this must not be done; because it is a very high substance until such time as there is no excuse to extract it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is compelled to extract [the tooth], it is necessary that you are certain of which tooth causes pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain leaves the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and have the good tooth extracted; yet still the pain does not leave because of this, until the bad one is removed, for we have already seen this with these sufferers; and when you are sure which tooth causes pain, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with all your might using a sharp spatula to protect the gums from all sides; then move [your instrument] with your two fingers or subtle forceps at the first point of contact, prying open until it is well loosened, then firmly close the forceps; and let the head of the patient be on your knee between your knees, holding them steady so they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it cannot be done, then take one of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, moving it like you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is perforated and worn down, you must fill it with small pieces of cloth where the hole is; then gently extract it with forceps so that it does not break during extraction; and one must work very carefully around the gums to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be careful not to break the tooth and leave a piece behind, as it may cause even greater pain for the patient due to the remaining root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware of not acting like the ignorant surgeons who, due to their haste and boldness, sometimes break the jaws and fail to manage what we have described; instead, they cause great harm to the roots that remain or the broken jaw, as we have often seen; when the tooth is removed, wash the area with wine, oil, and silk; if there is bleeding, which often happens, fill the space with powdered vitriol; if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, with which one moves teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so they do not double when you extract the tooth; these are the forms.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick metal, well-crafted, to prevent bending during extraction, and have teeth so as to hold the tooth firmly.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, you must place moist cotton soaked in butter over the wound for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is softened, you can then insert the tongs called "algefri", which look like a stork's beak; they should be shaped like this inside:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called 'althali', that is, a scalpel, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with this, it is good; if not, then assist yourself with all the instruments, of which the shapes are shown hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one assists with this instrument that has two blades, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front of the teeth's root, and this instrument which resembles a large pair of forceps, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be kept intact so that they do not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; also other instruments which are not listed here; the wise subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their works and the illnesses show them because of such diverse diseases as ancient ones didn't teach about any instrument for this; if one breaks some bone or part, then look for the corresponding instrument that is needed, as I told you, and study the gestures of which here follows its form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be big and sturdy to hold the bone firmly so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; then restore its place with suitable medicines for this purpose, and if there is decay in the bone which is small, remove it completely using all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, and the form is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you must know whether the tooth is newly born after the other teeth, and it is not in its rightful place, nor can be healed or limed; therefore remove it. And if it has air with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape resembles a small beak, made of sharp iron at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And use the hammer often and strike it with bare hands for its hardness against that of teeth, and so you do not move the others; if it appears possible to lime it, then take this lime whose form is as such:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	which is like the lime used to make needles; and you must lime this tooth often with bare hands gently so it does not move when biting; then finish it off at the end with any sort of razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then lime its sharpness until it is even, such that it neither hurts the tongue nor disturbs speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When front teeth loosen due to impact or fall, and the patient cannot bite down without them falling out, even after treatment with constricting medicines which is ineffective, they must be secured with a gold wire, as silver wire turns green and decays but gold does not change; the wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth; if you wish to align the teeth, take the wire and pass it double through two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth or teeth between them until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side; repeat this process covering the entire affected area, extract your hand carefully and gently so as not to move the tooth; secure the wire at the root of the tooth to prevent escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the gums of the filament with a pair of forceps, and assemble them, and put them back between the healthy tooth and the tongue, so that it does not harm the tongue; then leave it as tight as possible for as long as it can stay there, and if it loosens or the thread frays, tighten it again with another piece of thread; thus it will remain in place and serve its purpose forever, this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth and two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, one should put it back in its place, fresh for fresh, as we have said; and do not let anyone who is not skilled and patient intervene, and sometimes the form of a tooth is made from cow bone, and it is placed where there is a gap, and tightened as we have said, and thus it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut loose the tongue's tie
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	This is the tie that comes from beneath the tongue naturally or as an accident of healed wound; and to operate on it you open the mouth of the patient, have their head in your lap, lift up their tongue; then cut through the nervous tie widely so that the tongue is freed from its hold, and if there be hardness or knot due to sudden wound, insert a hook and cut this tie widely; take care not to go too deep for fear of cutting into the artery below; and when you have done it, wash the place with rose water and oil, or cold water, then put beneath the tongue a tent of linen; and let the patient hold their mouth open each night so that the wounds may not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If bleeding occurs, apply crushed vitriol directly to the site; if blood continues to seep, cauterize with the wart-removing iron, which is beneficial for this purpose; then treat it further until healing occurs.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you notice that it has turned pale or black in color and hardened to the touch without causing pain for the patient, do not touch it, as this indicates cancer; if it begins to turn white and moist, remove the crust with a spatula and clear away any moisture; if blood continues to seep during your treatment, apply crushed vitriol until bleeding stops, then return to your work until everything is treated; afterward, clean the site with linen and silk, and treat further until healing occurs.
des apostemes de la gorge	From abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never enter the throat boils that are called "godath", and properly we call them the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and false color, never touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, never touch it with iron, also due to the outflow of blood; but let it mature, and then you will remove it, or it would break on its own; and if it is white in color, runny, and the root is subtle, prepare your instrument for cutting, but first check if the abscess calms down and becomes peaceful.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, and his chiés soit en ton sain, and li oevre la bouche and lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, and presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue against all these instruments and see an abscess, take a lancet and insert it into the almond-shaped area, pushing as much as possible. Then pull anything that comes out with the needle back towards the instrument from which it originated; this results in a form resembling forceps. However, its tip is curved and has two sides, both sharp and made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have these instruments available to you, use regular pliers instead, which are shaped like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	One side is sharp while the other isn't, and when you have punctured one of the almonds following this method, do likewise to the other in exactly the same way. After making the incision, gargle with hot water mixed with wine or simply water; if blood flows then use only water for the gargling or boil pomegranate peels/bay leaves, etc., until bleeding stops. Then treat it until healed. Sometimes, other abscesses appear in the throat besides these two almonds so when this happens you must lance them just like the aforementioned pair of almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed inside her throat; specifically, the small type of abscess; it had almost completely blocked her windpipe so she could not breathe through it because it was obstructed, and neither could she eat or drink, and she would have died if we waited even one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess was so high up that two reeds had been placed through the nostrils to act as airways.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly grabbed a reed and inserted it into one of the nostrils, then pushed it upwards, and a large portion of bowels came out through the nose; then I repeated this in the other nostril, and opened the mouth and pressed on the tongue; after that I inserted the reed into the abscess and cut away a part of it, only some blood came out; thus we unblocked her windpipe so she could start drinking water and later wine, and I kept cutting from this abscess for a long time; however, the abscess would regrow, filling up the place that was emptied, until it became very big again; at which point I advised to lance and cauterize it inside the throat: then it stopped growing; I left these parts, trusting God to take care of her from there on.
de l’uve	Of the eye.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called a "perpendicular"; and if it is below large and round, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cleared as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the abscesses are eased, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and one which is round assembled and not long; and it is sanguine or of false color or black, then you must avoid its incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you seat the patient in front of the sun, and press their tongue with an instrument which we have previously mentioned; then insert the probe into the eye, and draw it out, and cut it with one of two instruments that I have mentioned for cutting almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut away flesh beyond what is superfluous and beyond the natural limit; for if you remove more, it harms the voice and speech; and after incision, use what we have said about incising two almonds, and treat until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears cutting, you should employ an engine for cauterization to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery is sharp fire.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And have the patient place their head in your hand, and then press their tongue with an instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and seal it with hot sharp fire, neither too thick nor too thin; and use this tool which is shaped thus:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this way, take calmness and hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, hawthorn, and similar herbs, and mix them all together or some of them in one pot, add oil to it, and boil; and the pot should be well-glued with strong clay, and inside the pot have a hollow instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or copper, and one end of the instrument is to be inserted into the patient's mouth so that the vapour rises through the throat until the uvula is withered; afterwards repeat this often, until the uvula dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess as many things can happen, and never perform it when there is a decline in a warm abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and place a piece of egg shell inside the patient's mouth so that their mouth does not become too hot; for the egg shell does not allow vapors to harm the mouth, and it is a good treatment along with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often something becomes stuck in the throat—a fish bone or some other object; therefore, you must extract what you can see and press the tongue down with a tool so that you may view the object; and for whatever does not appear and remains lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the object will be expelled by vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread; attach a string to the sponge and then have them swallow it; when it reaches the object, it will become attached, and you can then pull it out; if it does not come out by these methods we've mentioned, take an instrument made of bronze in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be bent towards the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised upwards; guard against touching the epiglottis lest vomiting occur or you push bone into it; better that the patient pushes the instrument in themselves because they know where the object is located; if he puts it inside his mouth, then pull on the entire instrument evenly until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	From the leech of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the leech medicine if I have not said so in my division of cures; and when this does not profit, then look into the patient's throat in sunlight, then press their tongue with the instrument that I mentioned to you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, draw it out with a very small hook, or use subtle pincers that serve this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hair plait and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert the end of the hair plait into hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient drink cold water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth and pour it in without swallowing, and move their hand frequently; as soon as the leech feels the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall out as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafetida, using the instrument I mentioned for smoking the eye; do this multiple times, for it will fall out without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot with live coals, and cover it with a perforated lid in the middle, and through this hole place the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation into it, and have the patient put the end of the cane in their mouth, closing their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but instead goes down to the phlegm; now the phlegm will be expelled, and if it is not, repeat the fumigation many times; let the patient suffer from thirst, eating salty things, and have them refrain from drinking water; then through this treatment the phlegm should exit.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to remove phlegm is like a pair of curved pincers designed to enter the throat when one can see it; and they have the appearance of a bird's beak, with a roughness similar to that of a file, so whatever it grasps cannot be released; here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses based on the descriptions that will follow in this book, and they vary according to their penetration and size; they can be classified into two types, one depending on its appearance itself, and another due to the moisture it holds.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second type is according to their location in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because abscesses of the head are different from those of the anus, and abscesses in fleshy places differ from those that occur at joints, each requiring its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And one should not lance an abscess if the bowels are weak according to their condition; but for those that must be lanced when they are ripe, and do not weaken due to their condition, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess forms near a joint, and it is left to rot away, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near a main limb, and if you delay perforation until it dies, it will harm the principal limb; when it is near the foundation, pierce it before it dies; and one must not puncture an abscess formed without digestion completed, unless that which is near the foundation rots away entirely, forms a fistula, and cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for perforating an abscess that is dead based on its development, and this is when pain subsides, fever breaks, swelling reduces around the abscess, and there is less agitation and sharpness of head of the abscess, along with other signs; and one should make the incision at the lowest point of the abscess, where it begins to move; and the perforation should be in line with the length of the body, and if the abscess is on hands or feet, or near joints and nerves and arteries, and all similar places where there is no bending.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in fleshy tissue, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed as digested and complete, just as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the poison would be elongated and filled with much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must bring small abscesses with small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many incisions according to the resemblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that require cutting through, when it is soft like cloth, and has become numb, then one must act as for boils: and there are those that are divided into three angles, and there are some that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, just like abscesses from sores; and there are those where you make a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuttings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, just as in a soft superficial abscess, you must fully pierce it; and when the abscess is large, and it has formed a great bow, and you pierce it, do not extract all of the bow at once, but take out a part; then stuff the abscess until the next day, then remove something from it again; do this several times gradually, until the entire bow comes out; especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or decrepit old men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit jumps sometimes with the release of the bow, which may cause the patient's death, and you will not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Examine this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then dry the wound, and observe if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a full incision, place linings of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many perforations, you must insert a lining in each one so that they touch each other; and if you have cut away part of the skin around the abscess, fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold and clear water nearby, wet the cloths, and place them over the bleeding area multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply compresses and a poultice, using the powders I mentioned previously in this book, and if it is wintertime, and the area or abscess is very sensitive, then you should place warm tents and cloths moistened with wine and oil; but if it is summertime, and the area is fleshy, then use cold water and oil on wet cloths, or wine and cold oil, for up to three days as we have said; afterward, unbind the abscess, dry it, and treat it appropriately until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head of the chief comes small abscesses, and are manners of us that are in cloths, just like the neck of a hen, and there is much of similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture just like pulses; and of such kind which are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is such that you test all instrument which is called "entromissoire", from whence its form comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it holds moisture, they do it from above through the length [of the limb].
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, remove it carefully without leaving any skin where the moisture was contained, for it will return if nothing is left behind; then apply Egyptian ointment with cotton, if present; if not, use water and salt, pack the wound, and leave it until the next day; this will draw out what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and again on the third, until you are certain that nothing remains from the night; afterwards treat the wound with ointment appropriate for healing, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is in a fatty area, cut it open like this, lengthwise; and throw away the onions (pus), and remove the skin from all sides, and take great care to extract whatever hair lies beneath where it rests; and if the artery opposes you, then do as I told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Also treat the abscess if it is full of pus, by cutting and curing as I told you before.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting into the purulent abscess is easier, as it has little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And in some of these abscesses where there is no moisture, and here I speak of an abscess I cut open from the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, which could not be broken; if one had struck it with any implement, they would have made as much of a wound as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses occurring on the head, those that come near the child's crown and at the root of the ears, the incision should be made in the lowest possible position to let out the pus; and treat them as required.
des scrophules	Scrofula.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	These abscesses often occur on the neck and under the arms, as well as in the groin area, and sometimes appear elsewhere on the body; they are very numerous and interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	Each scrofula is properly contained within its own region, just like the knot and abscess of the head, as we have mentioned earlier; there are many variations of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some contain pus, while others are malignant and resistant to healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, in that place where you see a good arrangement for touching, et est semblans a la color dou cors, and it resembles the colour of the body, et muet de chescune part and quiet on each side, et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, and not dry at the nerves of the neck nor at the artery or the passageway, et n’est mie parfonde; it is not deep; si covient que tu la copes par desus, so you must cut it from above, et l’escorche de chescune partie, and peel each part, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, stretch the two lips of the wound with hooks, se tu en as mestier, if you need to, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; as we have said for abscesses of the head; et la trai poc et poc, and drag it a little at a time, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, and let the spatula not be sharp nor cutting, que li mains n’eschaipe, lest the hand escape, et ne voise trop avant, and don't go too far forward, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois. so that you do not cut what you mustn't.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not stop bleeding, apply ground glass in the wound, or some powders that stem blood, and compress the wound; leave it until the abscess is pacified, the wound softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Once the bleeding is stemmed, return to your work until you complete it; then examine with your index finger if there remain any small abscesses, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the abscess, you must not cut that abscess in its root but bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall by itself without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, then you must join together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no remaining superfluity due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you must proceed to cut the root of it, and draw out the fire, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For scrofulas that have superfluity, pierce it where death appears; and pierce it like the one mentioned before, depending on how it is, then apply ointments with bandages and similar things so that it does not corrupt what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with ointment to promote flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the operation for throat cancer; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their description.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with dislocation, it is necessary that the slit in the throat known as 'epiglottis' be avoided; and no aid should be given to them by this method, because all veins and passages of the patient are affected by abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in II amandres.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the passage of respiration, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must make an incision beneath three circles or four with a small cross-hatching between two of them or by means of the quantity of the incisions on the surface, not in the cartilage; and their skin is suitable for the sectioning of the epiglottis which has no flesh, and the vessels are deep therein.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he must stretch the skin of the throat entirely, then split open the heart until it reaches the windpipe; remove the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the esophagus as we have said; this is demonstrated by the interruption of the breath from the trachea which should pass through a whole location but does not due to its being interrupted, and through the defect in voice; leave the wound open for some time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed since you suspect strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and sew it entirely without the cartilage; then apply medicines which promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and breathing has ceased.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and they will inhale through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. Then they would instruct to close the wound and heal it, once it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young lady take one knife, and thrust it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found blood coming out of it, and I knew well that she had not cut a vein or any part of the throat, and wind was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed; there will be no harm to the lady other than her voice being hoarse, which shall return after a while; because of this I say that one need not fear incising the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	From the swollen throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "swelling of the throat", and it is a large abscess with a yellow colour, more common in women; and it presents itself in two ways: natural or accidental; where the natural type has no origin.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type presents itself in two ways: similar to what we call a "fatty tumour", and the other way resembles an abscess caused by arterial injury; and it is dangerous, one should not operate with fire unless on those that are small, first examine thoroughly: if you find it like our fatty tumours, without any veins attached to it, then cut it as one would cut a tumour, removing all its covering, provided there isn't much of it; cauterise quickly and treat as necessary until it is completely healed.
des nous	de us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways of addressing us exist, of which I will mention all the similarities; now it is necessary for me to explain all the differences between 'us' and 'issue'.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that 'issue' is heat and fever lasting until the ebullition passes, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains I syfac, which is its own sack and follows the colour of the body, and begins like a scab, and grows larger; and they are of two types, either dry or moist, and very diverse in colour as I have said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the head, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "entromissoire," according to its form as it will be presented in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to examine new abscesses is that you should take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core; this should be done according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the entromissoire and pay attention to what comes out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture comes out, whatever its color, treat it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes out, know that it is greasy, so make an incision in the form of a cross, take hold with forceps, and gently peel away the skin from each side until you get to the cot where it lies; pull on the healthy nut with the incised edges; if you cannot remove it whole, tear it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains in the wound, it will return many times; and if a piece of it stays there, and the blood troubles you, then fill the wound with sharp corrosive powders, bind the wound tightly, apply warm abscess-relieving substances on top, and treat it with other cures until it is healed; and if the nose bone is large, cut open the two lips of the wound, and cure it with something that encourages flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the bleeding vein is opposed to you or anything else troubles you, hasten and apply crushed vitriol to it, and leave it bound for two or three days until the wound becomes gangrenous, and stops the boiling of the blood; then return to cutting away what remains from the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the shapes of the instruments used for insertion, and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small; and there are three types called "albaret", and one called "breb", and these also have three sizes: large, medium, and small, to probe abscesses or fistulas; and they are like needles that cut sores, made of yellow brass, iron, or silver, but those made of black lead are better for probing fistula swellings; and they come in three sizes according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of uncinas are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium and small; some uncinas have two bends of three types each; others with three bends also exist, but in three different ways; we find yet other uncinas that only present one bend, although they too appear in three manners. All these kinds are necessary where they are placed.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are sharp and made in such a way that they do not cut the flesh other than on one side, thus avoiding damaging nerves or blood vessels while removing necrotic tissue; this is what we call a curette. Curettes come with rounded ends to avoid discomfort when opening abscesses, and there are three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see here. We only use these instruments in fleshy places such as the legs, arms, breasts, abdomen, or similar areas; sometimes we also make smaller ones resembling scalpels for stopping bleeding, according to this shape.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it back in place to heal by binding veins together, and arteries, and sometimes they return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, making them look like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and for those who wish to cure it, one must follow this form from point b. to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with healing meat, then join the two lips of the wound together with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs downwards, and is softened due to its size like in women, one should split it into two sections above, via two similar incisions; thus one part will hold onto another at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from point b. up to g.; then scrape away the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, then apply what we have said about stitches and powders, and whatever else is necessary for its treatment, until it is healed; if it isn't healed, or the incision hasn't been fully made because the patient won't rest still, or due to a loss of blood, you should fill the wound with moist cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; leave it there until it melts away flesh and fat, then treat it until it is completely healed.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that appear under the armpits are like hard scrofulas where there is pus, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those which contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire mass within the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat gently until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofula, treat it as we have said for cutting scrofulas, and if the wound goes deep, apply cauterization as mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of an artery's rupture
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is sealed, many abscesses may form, and likewise, the vein becomes swollen and abscessed; one can recognize this situation in that when it is for the artery, the abscess runs lengthwise perfectly; and when you feel it with your hands, you sense a constriction; and when it is for the vein, there are reddish swellings appearing; and it is foolish to cut into this abscess, especially when it lies beneath the axillae and jaws and on the neck and in many other places, as it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, you should avoid iron-based treatment, and similarly for those at the head, you must also avoid it; in the case of an artery swelling opening through the skin lengthwise, proceed by making a small incision with scissors, separating the artery from its surrounding tissues so that it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath it, piercing through to the other side, securing the artery with double thread at two points, as I have instructed for the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then compress the space between these two bindings with an introducer until all blood has escaped from this region, and untie the binding; then adjust the treatment so that it hangs loose, allowing the ligature to fall away; then treat appropriately following this procedure until healing takes place; if the abscess is due to a vein incision, make sure to grab as much of the abscess tissue along with some skin, insert the needle underneath the part you hold in your hand and pierce through, securing it there with double thread so that you draw it from the other side; then bind the abscess together like I told you previously, using thread binding one end of each of the two threads' ends to its own end (of the thread); if you are uncertain about whether blood is escaping or not, insert another needle into the entire abscess underneath all threads up until where the first needle pierced through and secure the threads at four points; then cut open the abscess so that superfluous matter escapes, afterwards remove the superfluous heart-tissue while leaving what is bound intact behind; finally apply a moistened cloth with wine and oil, providing treatment via tents and ointments until healing.
des apostemes des ners	From abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Likewise abscesses come to nerves when they are bruised or by excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And they occur more frequently in shoulders and fingers and everywhere there are joints, and it is a severe abscess, and its color resembles the body's color, and it is found in various positions causing pain; and when one tightly restrains it, the patient feels pain, and it is not complete in the body but below the heart; and it spreads out on all sides, neither forward nor backward, or below or above, and one that is in joints should not be cut with an iron tool: perhaps contraction would occur; and those that are on the head or forehead, treat with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut its root; if it is large, suspend it using a hook, peel it back, then remove it and stitch up the wound, treating it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Large boils hanging.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.
