Sometimes they occur in the belly and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance, with a subtle root and large head; there are small ones and very big ones; I saw a man who had two on his belly that looked more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had a fine root, were gently split open, and moisture flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six thirds, and for the work of incision, you must consider if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist with delicate roots; then cut it with a broad spatula, and have fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For cutting often leads to excessive loss of blood, and if you faint from it, then proceed quickly with cauterization; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision with iron, take a well-made linen thread, and tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the linen thread until you cut the artery, each by its means without effort; and if the roots are large, be afraid to cut especially in the belly, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return, then treat the wound, and make sure not to cut the vein which is of a reddish color and poor in sap and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an aggravated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the wound is fresh
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the wound comes from cauterizing a sore or fissure on the skin, and it is on the stomach with some of the bowels exposed, as can happen in other types of wounds, or there is blood flowing from veins or arteries like mentioned before, or due to windiness; and if it is through the rupture of the skin and the emergence of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles that of the body's color, and it is a light thing without pain, and emerges in diverse ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the emergence of the intestine, then it becomes more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers it retracts, and then returns, and perhaps it is squeezed, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue, and it becomes apparent when you press it with your hand, as it does not constrict; but if it is because of blood, then it shows through these signs: abscesses that are large and hard, fixed in place according to quantity; and if it is due to windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and the treatment depends on whether the appearance indicates arterial or venous bleeding, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You must leave the healing process.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For if there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance indicates an issue with the intestine or anus, you must instruct the patient to hold their breath and lie down straight; then bleed them all around the belly; command them to often rest between your hands; then go around the place that was marked with a palm's-length span; extend half of the abscess above along the length of the large inch; bind it tightly with strong thread or sturdy silk rope, leaving enough room for the knot outside; open up the other half of the abscess over the knot and put your index finger inside, seeking out the intestine; if you find it caught by the binding, undo it and push the intestine outside the belly; if you find an artery or vein, carefully go around them, then return to your work and take two needles with strong thread through them; put the two needles across what was pierced in a cross shape; drain the abscess over four places on the needles, and if it drains, remove the needles, leaving the place until it rots, allowing dead flesh to fall away by itself; or you can cut it when it is soft and rotten, then treat as required, finishing the abscess as we have said; drain any blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place accordingly, and bind it up.
dou chancre	The cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken about the appearances of cancer and how it should be treated with medicine, and how one must avoid using iron for its cure. Now we speak of cancer that is engrained in the marrow, and great caution is needed during its treatment. The ancients say that when a cancer is in an area where it can be scraped away like the breast or thigh and similar places, then it should all be removed as soon as possible at the beginning; but if it has grown large and old, one must not attempt to treat it for I have never been able to cure any. Nor has anyone else ever cured such a cancer before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, one must purge the patient of black bile once and then bleed them if they are obviously bloated. Prepare a good place for the operation by laying the patient down comfortably; next cut out all of the cancer with your knife, taking it away from every side without leaving any behind; let the blood flow until its finished, then wipe the area well with your hand or something to make sure no more is left coming out and if the flow of blood makes you think that an artery or a vein was cut, cauterize it so the bleeding stops. Then treat the wound with other treatments until it heals properly.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already mentioned in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the accumulation of water is formed, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is achieved through medication, and those cured by surgery; so it is written only. And you must not touch with iron in these two types: namely tympanites and yposarche, for they are mortal illnesses. Therefore when you treat this dropsy case which is called "eclites" using medicine, and the cure does not help, then consider if the patient is weak or has other diseases like constipation, stomach inflammation and similar things; do not touch them with iron because it is doubtful and dangerous. And if you see that the sick person is of strong constitution, having only dropsy but neither too young nor old, proceed as follows: lift the patient upright on your hands, and have assistants press his belly from below pushing the water to the lowest part of the abdomen, then take a spathula with spines like this
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be two parts cut.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	thrust a sharp point into it but not so deeply that it can reach the intestine when thrust in and cannot wound; then look to see if the dropsy is caused by a swelling of the intestines - if this be the case, you must make an incision three fingers' breadth above the navel on the right side: but if the disease lies in the liver, then let your incision be made on the left side of the navel; and if it lies in the spleen, let it be on the right. It is not expedient that the patient lie upon his back so as to allow the superfluities to flow into a weak place: but pierce all the skin with an instrument, thrust it through and raise your hand above all the spatumile between the skin and the muscle (as in skinning) to the extent of one nail or thereabouts; then make an incision in the muscle so that the spatula may reach the hollow place, which is the water-place: then draw forth the water, thrusting this instrument into it - here is the form of the said instrument.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Et is semblans a une caine d'argent subtil, and is d'arain ou d'archaut legier, and has en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d'une part, III pertus; and II d'autre part, and I d'autre; and is li chiés tailliez si com une penne, and c'est li forme de l'incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	au chief desus est li alemele, so that when the instruments come to the water, they descend now upon the instrument; empty it therefore by half or a third part, for if you empty more than is appropriate in this hour, perhaps the patient dies due to the resolution of their spirit from the arm, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death; but empty according to his strength, and according to what the dispositions of his strength signify, and his pulses; then draw out the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now for the heart which stops up the aperture that I spoke about, which you pierce in this manner; then renew the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw off a small quantity of water; do this each day, and beware of leaving so much as a drop of water behind.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient's condition, and leave too much water inside them, cure them by burying or placing them on warm sand, and through excessive sweating or baths and sun exposure, and restrict their drinking; then heal with drying medicines until they are dry, cauterize over the stomach and liver and spleen after removing the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or with a small one, or it is not properly positioned.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If necessary, pierce it with a very fine pointed tool in this way:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put the subtle lead plug in the hole, and leave it bound for three or four days; when he wants to urinate, remove the plug so that he can urinate, then replace it; perhaps this is not necessary because the urine which flows out will prevent the closure from remaining.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	For those whose hole is small, the lead plug is a treatment, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the hole in its place are deformed, as no one is born with the hole at the head of the penis, which means they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upwards; nor can they procreate because the matter cannot reach the uterus, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of this work is such that the patient often lies on their back; extend the head of the penis and its shaft like a feather's length so that the opening faces upwards as it should be; take care to prevent any bleeding which happens frequently, if it does happen then stop the blood with whatever stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Pimples on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albath comes to the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh; there are malignant and non-malignant ones; you must take them with a subtle hook, then cut and clean all of them, afterwards put on cotton moistened with Egyptian ointment; treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of a foul colour and smelly, you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it open, and if the ulcer is on its surface, with a part inside the skin and a part outside, then you must remove the part that is inside first; and when it is healed, treat what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, the surface of the shaft is not secured so that it is not pierced, and there comes blackness and corruption on its surface and in the glans; then you must remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster made from honey and flour with pomegranate bark and fig leaves, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help with two conditions combined: that is, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must insert a hollow reed into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin dries at the tip of the penis in those who are not circumcised, or due to wounds or abscesses, then you must peel off the skin with a sharp instrument so that the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if this is a severe matter to treat, then you must peel it with a spatula at some point between the tip of the penis and the skin, then separate carefully between them, and place a fine damp linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not dry out again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like the dislocations of continuity such as other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do our best work, and the most gentle for their wellbeing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, as it was not part of their law, and we have only acquired this knowledge through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For the majority of masters and surgeons performed circumcisions around the age of one, using forceps, and a single knife; they would remove their foreskin as it had two layers, sometimes cutting through the upper layer and leaving the lower one intact.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now you cut it back again, and the pain is double, and in the cleaning which is done there is not an assured point of the limb; and in the cleaning of the nail perhaps the iron escapes, and they run to work, and many times thus arise that they have no need of cleaning and I want it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning that is done with force to all the tight binding of thread I have found the goodness of experiment, for the force cuts equally well both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, you cut equally well in I all the tension; but let the thread be well tightened around the leather; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not making him tie the thread around the rod only, and then you can have him stand up in any way you please; then make him stand between your hands straight, and cover the forces with your hands or beneath your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the rod and blow into the heart, and pull it upward until the head of the rod is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that has gathered there, then tie at a sign the place with a double thread, then bind beneath I peg to another binding; and hold II fingers by the second binding with the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two bindings, then lift the heart upward quickly and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood run little by little, for this is the poison; and put powder on top and over the powder a cloth glued with an egg yolk cooked in rosewater, mixed with good fresh oil roses, and leave it there until the next day, and treat him another treatment so that he heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of forceps for emasculation is as follows: the two handles should be turned and sharp, and the handles should be as wide as the main part equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in emasculation occurs when the heart inside escapes through the incision; therefore, you must extend it to your nail, otherwise, the wound may fester; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then use pincers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and what is beneath the shaft becomes swollen, let it be until any festering heat subsides, then lightly peel back the skin; cut as much of it away as you can, while taking care to avoid damaging the shaft itself, which will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of recent wounds with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if it is cut too deeply from the heart, and it goes above, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	From retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or foreign body, or similar matters, which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is caused by a stone in the bladder neck, then the patient should be bent over their knees; place their feet on their back, extend their belly away from their back, and restrain the patient's testicles as much as possible; this will force the bladder neck to express the stone above it, so urine can flow out. If it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must perform extraction with all the instruments called a "syringe", of which this is its form: let it be made from thin silver like bird feathers; let the tube be one palm long and half wide, and be thin at its end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, and place the doubled string at the head with a pouch of wool or cotton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; and insert the head of the thread inside the syringe; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, then cut away any excess wool and push it up to the head of the syringe, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, and anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, and have the patient sit on a chair, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; then lubricate the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches its root, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; then bend the penis upwards towards the belly, puis boute la siringure avant jusc’a la vessie, and push the syringe forward up to the bladder, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; then have the patient feel it reach an empty place, and this is not done according to order unless the passage where it goes is twisted; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, and stretch out the thread with its entire wool pouch, et li urine en suit la laine, but the urine follows the wool, puis l’estrai fuer, then pull out the thread, et fai corre l’urine; and let the urine flow; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, and restart with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, et soit aligiez li malaides. and ease the patient's suffering.
des maladies de la vessie	Of bladder diseases.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood come into the bladder, where decay has gathered, and you see that water and medicine must be distilled within it, then make all the instrument which is called 'clepsydra', and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three apertures: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; and let the tube through which the medicine passes be such that it plugs well into the penis without addition, so that moisture can be drawn out of it, and blown in when necessary; and when you want to introduce your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the scent-bearer into the urine, and draw the air from within it; thus will you draw up the urine through the tube, then blow strongly back into it; so shall the urine enter therein and return now to the bladder, that the patient may feel it; this is the form of the subtle clyster wherewith we clysterise the bladder: thus it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or archaut, and the head is higher up; below at I chest level where the ligature falls; then take a sheep's bladder and place the moisture with which you wish to catheterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a good double thread, and heat I pot this moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the catheter into the urethra, then squeeze your hand over the bladder so that all the moisture flows in, until the patient feels that the said moisture has entered the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment paper, make it round like a circle and pierce it around; insert I strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles I thimble, and put inside whatever you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, press with your hand until the liquid comes out of the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the types of stones and their extraction along with medications; I have spoken about the difference between kidney-induced stone and all its symptoms, as well as which type of stone requires surgical intervention; and concerning the bladder, urethra and penis; now let me tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder occurs more often in children, and this is a sign that the urine resembles water due to its subtlety; it contains sand, and the patient experiences pain when urinating, which happens frequently, then stops; moreover, many have haemorrhoids with this condition; the recovery is easy for children up until four years of age, while it's very difficult in elderly people, and intermediate among those who are young adults aged between youth and old age; also, treating large stones is easier compared to small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the bile that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes obstructs when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by their feet, lift them up and move them backwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from above; then have him sit down between your prepared hands, with his hands below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then search for it and feel inside; if you perceive the stone in this space, now be quick to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall when touched at all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or with your middle finger, if he is an adult; and insert it into his anus, seek out the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, direct it towards the neck of the bladder; then press upon it with your finger, and push it outside where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch with his right hand the cords upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the cords in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatula, which has this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Make an incision between what is between the cords and the fundament, not in the middle but at the left side of the navel; let it be straight over the stone, and your fingers should be close to or touching the fundament, and make the incision so that it is wide on the outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, but not too large; perhaps the pressure will push what is at the fundament out without effort; and know that there are some stones with angles and margins: they are difficult to remove; and others which are underneath, similar to a pea, and round, whose exit is gentle.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must take care of it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine returns through an opening that the flesh cannot close; still try to extract it, either by pulling or crushing with forceps, until you remove it in pieces; and when you have finished your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, compress it, and apply a moist cloth with oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then have the patient lie on their neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess appears in the wound and there is corrosion, and blood coagulation in the bladder, causing urine retention that is known to come out with urine: so push your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will inflame the bladder, and it will rot; then cleanse the wound with water, oil, and linen, and treat it in all ways you know until it heals; and every time you treat it, bind his two thighs together, and gather your medicines at the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	When you forge an iron tool according to this form, it should be three-pronged and fixed onto a pole:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. de la piere des femmes	Of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes a stone forms in women's bodies, and if it happens once, the treatment is difficult, and it is prohibited for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that we cannot find a suitable female expert who can expose herself to view, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the symptoms, you can predict the outcome.

de hernie carnouse	Of hernia, fleshy.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramusaceous water is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white serous fluid, which lies beneath the heart of animals and contains the egg; it is called 'serous fluid', and sometimes is properly within the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that this could be another egg; it is the skin of the animal between the white serous fluid we mentioned; and they do not know its name.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramusaceous fluid is due to weakness that comes in animals, and this matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor. Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant. de l’aposteme des coions	From the abscess of testicles

It is necessary that you have the patient sit on an elevated seat, then tie the testicle support below your thumbs to all the vessels that are near the penis, hold them firmly, and stretch them out forcefully; then cut transversely with a broad cutting spatule through the covering of these vessels until they are exposed; after which skin from each side as we have said when extracting arteries in the temple; insert a needle there where you had the double thread and tie it at the first place where the vein came, and again to the other end; then cut them right down the middle along the length of the body removing the corrupted moist humors; after which cure the wound as with others that one is going to sew up so that no vessel dies on account of one testicle, because through this there comes no harm, and if in all the vessels there is a vein then it is necessary to remove the testicles from all the vessels; so that the urethra does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, dry up, and be unable to help itself.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the fracture of the skull.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are due to the fracture that occurs in the skull or the extension on the abdomen in the region of the groin, which causes the intestines to descend from this fracture into one of the scrotums; and this fracture is either of the skull itself or its extension, and these two types come about through many causes: blows, jumps, falls, lifting heavy weights, and similar things; when it's an extension of the skull, the signs are that it occurs gradually over a long period without coming suddenly; and the abscesses are formed equally around towards the surface because the skull pushes against the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it's a fracture of the skull are that it causes sudden pain at first, and there are various abscesses appearing below the skin close by, which is due to the protruding intestine and body above the skull.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the muscles slip down with the intestine, and they are trapped there, causing great pain to be endured by the patient, especially when pressed upon.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron cure procedures with fear, it is necessary to withdraw from them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of this procedure is such that you instruct the patient to draw their intestine up with their hand into the wound if they are able to reach it; then be mindful of its place on your neck between your hands, and lift their thighs; then stretch the heart upwards, and remove all skin from the upper part of the scrotum; then push in the forceps of the size you need to open up the wound so that the testis may come out; then peel off the white tough skin covering everything; then put your index finger into what joins the testicle where it is between the white skin covering and between the second skin, and separate that which is behind the testicle, and between the second skin; and with your right hand move within the heart of the scrotum, stretch the white skin upwards with your left hand, and lift up the testis along all the skin towards the wound; and command an assistant to stretch the testis upwards, and loosen what is behind it, bind it there. Then look for yourself at your fingers if any part of the intestine has been wrapped in the tough skin, and should you find anything put that down into the belly below; then take a needle with thread as thick as four threads, put the needle through the rear part of the skin which comes after the skin covering the scrotum behind the wound, and cut off the strings so there are four remaining. Gather together these ends one above another in cross formation and bind this tough skin we have mentioned which is below the skin of the scrotum with a strong binding of two parts; then wrap the ends of the threads around and tie them tightly into two parts such that none of the vessels that feed it can enter through, so that no abscess may come there. And put again the bandage as along the first long one for two fingers of this, and after these two bindings leave from the skin which is below the heart of the scrotum a distance equal to a finger; and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is below the skin covering the scrotum such that blood may flow out, as we have said before. Then take moistened wool in oil, put it into wounds and bind with thread of which we have spoken above.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white skin we mentioned is cauterized after incision due to fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leave the cord until it breaks by itself; and if it delays falling off, let it be bathed in warm water, and apply what we mentioned above until it breaks; then treat the wound with another remedy until it heals perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch which bears the fig, in such a way that you bind the vessels lightly beneath after cutting above; then cut into the middle and treat the abscess of what festers until the vessels fall away; and treat it as we mentioned before until it heals.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Some times rupture comes in the groin as we have said and its place becomes visible ; and no intestine descends into the scrotum , but if it does descend , this is little, and it will repair every hour  ; however , if it remains too long at this point , then ulcer grows or fistula so that the intestine descends; and this happens due to extension of the fistula which comes in groin as we have said because it extends , after which the skin becomes soft and swells and its place appears ; and cure is by cautery like we already told you before ; sometimes it can be cured with an iron tool in the following way : sick person lies on back between your hands then cut that swelling of rupture at groin according to size of three fingers; next pull out fistula which is underneath skin , then take a rod or iron bar and put it above place of fistula ; press it against abdomen, then incise two places of fistula over the head of the rod and incise both one after other; next pull out the head of the rod but do not cut anything off from fistula nor extend egg nor any other thing , as I already told you in cure of intestines prolapse ; then cure it by wound treatment
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat sons' injuries, clean them and heal the wounds until they are healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The incision is restricted, and has no appearance on the surface, and cauterization is suitable in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	softening of the skin around the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin around the joints becomes soft in some people because the tissue underneath is softened and visible; it needs to be treated by making the patient lie on their back, then cutting away the softened skin above healthy skin; then join the two edges with a single stitch, and if you wish, sew the redundant softened skin together with three or four strong stitches; then cut between the sutures and treat like other wounds until healed, removing the thread.
dou chastrement	Of castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castrations are forbidden in our law, and for this reason, I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and there is no necessity except for two reasons: one is so the doctor can know how to respond when asked about it and know its cure; the other because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, calves and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say that castrations are performed in two ways: either by extraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we perform by extraction, we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles are softened and hanging; then grab them with your hand until they are removed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: you must hold the beast and press its skin around the testicles with your left hand, then tie a suspender, cutting each testicle once with one stroke when they are well skinned; leave some of the coarse fat and fine fat which is on the vessels; this method of castration is safer than that done by traction because sometimes something remains of the testicles through which the animal desires lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	D’hermaphrodites: de those who have both male and female sexual organs.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	An hermaphrodite is of two kinds in men: one is when between the two testicles appears a sort of natural figure like that of a woman where there may be hair and sometimes urine comes out.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another type of dislocation occurs in women, affecting the wrist as if it were a rod with two joints.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The treatment for men and women is to join the separated parts together, and treat them like other wounds; in the second case, of men whose urine escapes through the skin of their joints, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	Of stings
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A sting is a separated part of the body on a natural surface, so ugly to see; some women have them as big as a hand, and that is their treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must hold the excess of the sting in your hand or with tongs, and cut it lightly; do not go too deep to avoid bleeding, then treat any other wound until they are healed; there is another type that appears on the skin's surface, swells up, and may burst, appearing like a cow, so the ancients called it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it off as we have said for gangrene, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de erratique	Of wanderers
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Wandering is the case when the woman's nature is not perforated, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident due to illness that has occurred; or it is caused by a narrow passage, or a subtle syphon or species, and it is located perfectly in the middle, or on the sides, or below, or wherever; and prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly the flow of menstruation; and knowledge of such a case is obtained through examination of the bath.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the obstructions are close to each other, use your fingers or a rod.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a delicate fistula and close to the two lips, hurry up and do this: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two lips wide apart so that the delicate fistula is rounded, and cover the stitches; then take wool, dampen it in oil, and put it on the spot, and make the woman lie with the man every day until it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the fistula is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula similar to myrtle leaves.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stitches are made of fresh wood, suspend them with a thread and cut them; and have wound-healing medicines ready such as dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white; then bring a wide piece of leaden cloth so that the wound cannot heal; and let it be like this for a long time, and provide him with a dry linen dressing; then treat other treatments until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is fresh flesh in the wound, it must be cut according to this method, unless there are deep-rooted abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the deep-rooted abscess in the wound, one must not apply any treatment involving fire.
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood normally flows, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; I have already mentioned their similarities to others, as well as the signs, and now I will speak of those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and hard growths, when they are completely inside the anus and cannot be felt, should not be treated with fire cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, where one can feel it, they are those whom one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You must therefore put the woman in a cold house, then extend the ulcer with tongs and cut it at its roots, then powder over medicines that restrain blood, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; next, press her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate peel, galls and similar substances, then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg white, and apply this as an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have him undergo cupping on his back and breasts without wounding; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or juice of agrimony with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the abscess has healed, treat the area with ointment until it is cured; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so you must cut it as I said for the thululeh; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses of the navel
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many types of abscess that can occur in the navel, such as cancer, stony abscess, herpes, cysts, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscess, and several other diseases I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which appears on the buttocks, which is not one of the abscesses that fall off; and if you want to know how to treat it with iron, look to see if the abscess is acute at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not hasten to pierce it, but let it die until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat, and place two small seats where he can lean, supporting his back and bringing his feet towards the parts outside the legs; and let his thighs be spread apart, placing his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good bandage. Then suck it out toward the right side of the buttock, and bring in the instrument used to open the mouth of the abscess, which will then form into an ulcer, and when you use this instrument make sure to gauge its depth first so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than necessary, and that it does not hurt the patient. If the instrument is larger, cover the bottom of the abscess with a cloth so that the instrument does not harm him; and have someone hold the handle of the instrument while you use it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and it is softened by hand, you must cut at its head, or with a spatula-like tool; and when the bowels are emptied, then you should place moistened bandages soaked in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound; put the bandage beneath the wound onto the bone, and cover over the bone and wrist with clean linen cloth dampened in water or boiled mallow; treat after two days of this treatment to ensure healing; sometimes lift the bone and wound by cleansing with water and honey, and then with water or boiled lily root and aristolochia longa; return to ointment application.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is deep into the bone, then you must be careful of burning with iron, but treat it as we have said in this section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first to know the appearance of natural childbirth and its signs which are when you see the woman pressing downwards and wanting to smell things: then the child hastens to come out forcefully; therefore, know that these labours are according to a natural pattern, with the exit being under their head, and the midwife assists them; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press on her belly so that the baby comes out quickly; for when they descend face first, then the midwife assists them, and the husband is delivered of his superfluities by good circumcision; those who come otherwise do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.
