For it sometimes comes out feet first, and the body or head comes out forcibly, or the hands come out first, or it emerges from her belly, or often the child is turned onto its neck, and by other bad presentations; thus it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the presentations how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out headfirst due to natural delivery, and the woman gives birth with great difficulty, and her strength is weak, have her sit on a saddle or be held by the women; stimulate her nature with oil from fenugreek which has been cooked, then insert the small spatula provided between her two palms.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	Cut the amniotic sac and scratch at her nail until the moisture which is there flows out; press on the woman's belly so that the child descends; if it does not descend, you must administer an enema to the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and sesame oil; then have her sneeze from snuff and hold her mouth and nose for one hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out first, you must gently push them back in a little at a time; and if they cannot be pushed back in, place the woman on a chair with her feet raised above her head; then lift the chair off the ground, holding onto the woman so she does not fall when standing up; and if the hands still cannot go back in, and the child is dead, cut its hands with the knife provided here, extract the child, and reposition it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the baby's birth upon its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on its feet, you must push it upwards; and then turn it over and over until it is equalized; then take one of its feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to the thighs, instruct them to grasp and make them sneeze gently; if they jump further, may God will it so.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not so as we have said, turn it over and over until it is according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come as we have said, take some mucus from a cow's nose, and oil of sisymbrium, and melted gum, and grind everything together in a mortar; put this on the woman's nature inside and outside the ointment, then make her sit in tepid water up to below her ribs; and when she is moistened beneath, make her a collar of myrrh, and place it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and press her belly gently, for the child jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	On the birth of the child onto their knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, place a pillow beneath their hands, one on each side; then let her lean over and hang the baby's feet down; let it lie on the bed; bend its hands back, first one way and then the other; then take hold of its hands under the belly, remove the cushions from underneath until she is fully extended downwards; if the child does not squirm, take his feet and move them strongly, then move his stomach upwards, then place both your hands over his head; rock the baby backwards and forwards; and tell the woman to keep still so that the infant can come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	On the birth of the child, when one hand comes out sideways
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must devise a way to bring back the hand: if one cannot do it, then have the woman get up and walk; if she can't walk, make her lie on the bed, with her legs firmly extended; next, apply the warm compress I described; and if she does not give birth, sit her on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; finally, deliver the child naturally, have her sneeze, and tell her to push as long as the baby is coming out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the baby's exit onto its neck, spread her arms wide, and turn her face towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I must ensure the nurse holds her hand, then turn it gently back and forth, and move it slightly; once it is even, apply a natural warm compress with oil as we discussed earlier, then instruct her to move little by little; after you have done this, sit her on a chair, tell her to push; make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	Of this same manner throughout all of secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it happens forcefully in this manner throughout secondine, cut the secondine with your nail, so that the moisture is drained; and if the child presents itself on its face or neck, remove it from there, making sure it is not trapped, and turn the child; then push the child inside until you have positioned it correctly, and tell the woman to hold still: then extract it gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the twin's birth
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes even three or four are born; this is not a strange occurrence, but an event that happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Those which are strange things, and do not live at all, if they have a name; I know that they multiply, and are separated by the soft surface which divides them, which is attached to the swelling; and sometimes they also come out naturally like any other, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out violently, then treat it as we have said, and let the doctor be skilled, and act quickly and lightly in what he does; and do so as is best for healing.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all shaped like a child by the measurement of the glorious blood, and it is necessary that the doctor know all this, because perhaps similar things may happen to him; so he should act accordingly as required.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman for a dead child in her womb, as I explained earlier, and it doesn't come out naturally, and you have to perform manual work; you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; the woman should be placed on her back, with her hips inclined downwards, and legs raised; the assistant holds her in two places, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not disturbed during the delivery of the child; then rub the mouth of the deceased with moist oil mixed with a poultice of althea and fenugreek seeds, and linseed; grease your hand with these oils and poultices; then gently insert your fingers into the vagina, while making sure that the child does not descend onto its head; if it is stuck in its eyes, neck, mouth, palate, under the beard, forceps or near the sides, and if the descent is on the feet, use a hook and midwives; you should hold the hook with your right hand, put the curve between two fingers of your left hand, insert it gently into her entire hand, and place the hook in any of these places we mentioned until the body comes out empty; this is the shape of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert it into the other notch or hole as needed so that the extractions are even; then stretch them evenly by pulling from one side and then the other, to take out splinters, and have the notches notched for holding, as follows:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, coat the patient's finger with oil and push it into that area; pull out the other part; and if no splinters remain, place this notch or hole higher up, and do so until everything comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and it cannot be pulled back due to constriction, you must wrap them in a cloth until they are entirely covered; then cut through at the joint of the palm or with a knife, and do likewise for the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is standing on its feet, then the traction is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the womb is also light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is cramped in the belly or breast, you must extract it with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and tear open the belly or breast until the moisture that is inside runs out; and if other parts are delivered but the head remains, then insert your hand as far up as possible into the womb, and pull [it] down to the mouth of the womb; then insert one or two fingers, and draw it forth; and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to hot inflammation that has developed there, you must not labor at all but must apply moistening and greasy things; he applies ointments, and these are made with soft and moistening liquids.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is lying on its side, and you can put it in a straight position, follow what we have said for the living child; but if one has no power over it, then tear it limb from limb, leaving nothing of the placenta behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	Once you have done this, follow what we have said for hot abscesses that appear in the vagina; and if there is an outflow of blood, let it be put in cold water while restraining movement, and treat with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a child had died; then another was born on top of it and the other one also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess formed in the buttocks and swelled until it burst open, beginning to produce great pus.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat [him], and I thought for a long time, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong attraction, and from it came out one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly astonished because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it might be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I felt the wound and drew out several bones until the woman was much improved; she lived for a long time with only one part of her intestines missing, but otherwise healthy; I have recorded this chapter because when masters find an unusual case they should know how to offer assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the marrow back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressure device, for which we have the cords; and again to the heads of these two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more refined than those of the pressure device and made of ebony or boxwood; the mouth of the trunk is two fingers wide and its border one finger thick, while it is a palm and a half in length; between these two lines are two adjustments made from this same piece of wood that must measure a half-palm long or a little more. These two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open when you turn the horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar in its refinement and lighter to the previous one is made of ebony or boxwood resembling a pair of tongs; it has two adjustments at either end that measure a palm long and are two fingers wide; when you want to open the marrow with this whole device have the woman sit on a bed with her feet hanging down and legs spread then insert the two adjustments together into the marrow and hold the head of the instrument underneath between their thighs; move your hand along the length of the instrument as if you were using tongs in equal measure, according to how much you want to open the mouth of the marrow so that it does what she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all surmounted, and their appearances are multiplied; and when the surgeon has them prepared, it makes his work faster, and more valuable to men for its quality.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair if you do not have the instrument prepared, for their necessity is inexcusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the midwife is delayed in childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze forcefully, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; if she faints from this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in its lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the sufferer inside, such as wormwood, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia and centaury; cook all these herbs or some of them in water over fire; then place one end of the pipe into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the sufferer, and hold it there until the vapours go inside the sufferer; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If there are multiple injuries, treat them as a single wound.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if the second degree remains after this treatment and does not subside, instruct the assistant to moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or muskroot juice, and then insert it into the body, searching for the second degree; once found, she should grasp and extend it little by little in a straight line so that the edges do not tear during extraction; but it must be moved lightly right and left, then pulled; thus it will come out and separate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the opening of the wound is narrow and constricted, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing and herbal fumigation; and if it does not heal with all that we have said, take care not to tear during pulling; instead, you must tie what is at the mouth of the wound to the thigh of the woman, then administer a clyster of four-fold ointment; this will soften and reset it, causing the injury to heal; but nevertheless, when softened, there may arise foul odor in the stomach and head, injuring the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So, therefore, appropriate fumigations for this are: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers (menstrual flow) and the secundines is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass, similar to a cane, and the subtle head (of the instrument) goes into the nature (substance being heated), and its ends are broad over the fire; and let the fumigation be over the coals until it is spent, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce (the) fundament(s).
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their fundament pierced, but rather it is closed with a subtle membrane; therefore, in the bath one must pierce this membrane as they should and not use a sharp spatula to perforate (it), and take care that the midwife does not touch it; then apply moist wool soaked in wine and oil, and treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, insert a plug of lead into the hole, and leave it there for several days; remove it when the child wishes to go outdoors.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Sometimes this blockage occurs suddenly in a wound or abscess; you must cut away the blockage and treat it as described above with the lead plug.
de la fistule dou fondement	Concerning anal fistula, when pus comes from deep inside...
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulae which come from underneath the anus are called nodules, and those that appear on its surface or in between these two areas may be one fistula or multiple; when this nodule is old it opens up and reveals moist white pus or worms, and sometimes these fistulae penetrate deep; they can be recognized by the person who has them either during defecation or flatulence, and occasionally a worm may jump out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate up to the bladder, and halfway through the penis; they reach as far as the hip joint, and even to the knee bone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	Thus one can identify whether the fistula penetrates through the anus or not: put your index finger at the anus and insert a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula, when there is no torsion.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is torsion, insert a slender tent made of lead or horsehair into the fistula until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it and no excretion or wind comes from the opening as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; refrain from treating.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula perforates up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, urine leaks out of it, and it cannot be healed by medication.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated up to the hip joint, then the path goes down there; if there is no tortuosity and the cause of pain is nearby, then one should go straightaway with a knife, and neither medicine nor ointment will work quickly; in these perforating fistulas, there is no cure other than surgery, and it is vain folly for quacks to attempt it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those that are not perforating and are not old, there is hope of healing with iron, as I have experienced, and the patient should be lying between your hands on his back; lift their legs up to their thighs, then bend their thighs towards the belly; put in a bronze probe or an iron one if it is tortuous, until you know where the path lies.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, you must insert your index finger, and if you then feel that the tendon has been pierced; and if you can feel between your finger and the skin or flesh, know that it is perforated; do not labor over it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can indeed heal some of these cases, but this happens rarely; and the help given consists in heating the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as described above; and inserting it hot into the fistula until it reaches near the anus; do this twice or thrice until you know that the faulty flesh is burned away, which resembles a bird's feather; then treat with moistened tents in butter so that all the flesh comes out, after which treat with healing ointment joining flesh and sealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this method cannot be used to heal him otherwise; and if the fistula tries to enter but does not reach the very bottom of the anus, place your finger between the tent-like fistula and cover it with a thick layer of fat or suet, and you will see the fistula through this covering on the heart side; then cut off from the start of the fistula and push forwards before the tent, and cauterize afterwards until reaching the head of the tent; the tent will be relieved and fall out; then remove those faulty flesh bits that look like a bird's feather, leaving nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood beats you and cuts between your finger and the work, then cauterize with fire or astringent medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauterization combines two beneficial effects: the burning of adjacent flesh and the stemming of blood flow and drying of moisture; then treating wet wounds with butter or ground substances until the skin puckers and contracts over the burnt area; next treat the wound with healing, softening salves that harden into firm scar tissue.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Once it is reset, it is healed and will not dislocate again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	If the fistula reaches deep into the anus, and is far from the body's edge, insert your finger into the anus and feel around for it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tumor and find skin or a membrane or flesh that is about to burst, use only methods that offer hope of survival; cauterize as mentioned before, cut deeply, or apply medicine that will shrink it; don't go too deep lest you sever the muscle that holds up the anus leading to involuntary discharge; then treat it as described earlier. Maybe it'll heal, or remove the covering and clean it after cutting near the anus with ointment or sharp instrument; then scrape away bad flesh from the wound as much as possible; finally work on healing the wound and stopping the fistula outside of the anal area: this would be less painful for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are formed in this manner: it is when you insert a tent into the fistula, and it lies on the side of the fundament near the skin above, then take a perforated tent at its head in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And there insert the thread awry in [II], and insert the tent along the entire thread into the fistula until it reaches its head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it has pierced through the margin of the fundament internally, then withdraw the thread from that hole, such that you insert your finger into the fundament; and pull out the head of the thread, and join both ends together, and press one to the other, and let it sit for [I] day or [II]; and sometimes restrain it, until the thread gathers its flesh which is between them, and excretes; then treat the wound until it is healed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, make it burst in every way you can, unless it is too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make an incision so deeply embedded, then treat it with a bandage, as we have said, until it heals.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the sharp-spouted spoon which is used to make the fistula is very pointed on one side and cutting on the other; and not on the other part, for it does not cut what should not be cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	From hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like grains of pitch, and there are small and large ones, and they flow with blood, and there is one or more of them, and they are outside the anus and at its head; but those which are outside have little moisture, and moreover, they contain a bit of yellow water or a bit of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is that you instruct the patient to strain themselves in order to go to the toilet, until the anus remains open, and its edge becomes visible; you then hurry up and grasp it with pincers, or hold it at your nail, then cut it at its root; and if the pincers cannot hold them due to their moisture, then take them with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather; and pull them out with your two fingers, then cut them, and put some hot powder on top which serves as cauterization; or you can cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, afterwards treating them with other cures until they heal; and if the anus cannot be opened, then administer to the patient a sharp and bitter clyster in order to wash what is inside the anus, so that it may open widely; when the patients strains themselves, and if the edge of the anus becomes visible, then the treatment is light; and you take them with your nail or pincers, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they heal, and avoid incising with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	For drying of feces or from the anus
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying of feces in the intestine, either due to natural constriction or when the illness is old and medicine has no effect.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Use a spatula or your nail to scrape off the bark-like layer on top, ensuring it does not become moist; then treat it until it hardens as required; if it cannot harden, repeat the scraping more vigorously than before, until it heals greatly and becomes scarred; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of swelling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formix is a small faulty appearance between the body and goes very deep; sometimes it finds coldness, and one feels swelling like death, and it spreads throughout the body, especially in the hands more than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a reed made from a goose quill, or a strong vulture feather, and place this reed on the trembling, so that the purple rings touch the trembling all around; then turn your hand over the entire reed until you clasp it all around the trembling, and place it perfectly, uprooting the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one from a reed of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be subtle below and straight above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold with your thumb and forefinger, and you must compress [it]. And if you wish, cauterize the trembling as we have said before in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	One time the clyster is made of silver or quicksilver, or melted tin or lead alloy; and one time these instruments are small and large, according to those for whom they have been prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These therefore which are used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and suffer pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster, small and large, is above broad, where the bellies are bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it has an outlet where the bellies are bound, as you see, and the head is pierced inside it; and have on one side two perforations, and on the other one; and be the bellies or what we put the medicine in of a beast's bladder or parchment, and be perforated all around with small perforations, and have between each perforation one finger-width of space, then push into these perforations one strong thread of twisted twine in the form of an X or tied around it; and gather together the belly as if it were a goat's stomach; and when the medicine is inside, tie it with a strong thread to the instrument before you clysterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg white, or something similar, then gently insert it; then have the ministers press his II hands together until everything is visible, then remove the enema, and raise the patient's legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, hold on as much as you can; and if he sleeps a whole night there, so much the better.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him for a bellyache, and the medicine wants to come out quickly, then start again until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there are hemorrhoids at the anus or abscesses, then let the enema be as gentle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which the skin is drawn up.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed the treatment of wounds; now we will explain the healing process and the medical approach accordingly.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are caused, where they are located, and what has caused them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are caused by various things such as striking with a stone, sword or knife cuts, or injuries from a lance, stick or arrow, or similar objects; they can also be classified according to the body part affected, like wounds on the neck, head, foot, stomach or liver, and so on. I will explain the treatment for each type of wound, starting with simple head wounds since memory will come into play in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is due to a stone or similar objects, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large, and you slightly suspect of an abscess: make him bleed immediately with the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be contrary to the injured part; and let the patient abstain from overeating wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his diet be reduced, and let him neither drink wine nor eat meat; put on the wound, if hot abscesses appear, a moistened cotton in rose oil alone, or in styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, apply to the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not been moved by air, the powder which I will mention a little later; but if the wind has moved it, put on some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	Et if the wound is large like that of a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with sutures, then join them by stitching, as I will explain for wounds in the abdomen, at the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and flaps over, only attached by a portion of skin, then cut it off; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard tissue in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat solid meats, such as boiled beef, wheat porridge, poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrid flesh on the wound and it does not reach the bone, cut away all the rot, discard it, then treat the injury; and if there is a spurting artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, tie off the artery, and should you find it severed, bind it with thread; and if that does no good, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it consists of applying this powder which seals as soon as the wound has been cleaned.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The way of the powder is as follows: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts live alum, and finely grind them all together, then apply to the wound, pressing it firmly so that it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly, leaving it unbound if there is no swelling; for the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses only the live alum if there is no incense nor dragon's blood available, but the wound should first be cleaned.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has burnt the wound, especially during summer, do not apply this powder, but instead use some digestive ointments, or a poultice made of barley flour with water and honey until it forms a paste; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is minor, extract it with fine pincers; I will tell you about head fractures later on.
de la plaie dou col	On the wound of the neck:
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound occurs on the neck and it is straightforward, there is no significant difference between this and a head wound, but if the windpipe or artery in the neck is severed...
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other treatment than to leave them alone and put nothing constricting on them, as this harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuity is with the brain, which is the highest organ; but let the medicine be soothing, like warm water washed in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber also washed in soft water, and other stones of your choice according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it open and bind with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with hair and pus, cut it deeper at a lower level; and if the artery is severed, and blood flows out, open it up, clean it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the windpipe of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is preserved so that breath can pass through, then cut the heart above the pipe of the throat, but do not touch the throat itself instead restore it to its natural shape; and then bind it gently, leaving it a few days, before treating with drying ointments until healed; and if the wound has penetrated into the bone, clean it out; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them out forcefully if you can, and those that you cannot, leave for a while until the wound rots, and is relieved and soothed at its exit; and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder as I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has formed a fistula, treat it as I have described in its own chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, examine whether air rushes out of the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is deadly; but if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it nor bind it for the blood should not be stopped from flowing out fully, as this may return to the heart and kill the patient; instead apply an attracting ointment, and bandage twice a day; if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on their wound for three days or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor malignant tremor of the heart or breathing difficulties; and when you see these good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat her with tents and other treatments until she is healed; and if she cannot heal, operate, knowing that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife incision and it is simple, on the chest, or back, treat what is in front; if it is large, sew it up; if small, use powder; if it has penetrated the bone, and pieces have struck the bones, cleanse the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are loose; but if not loose, let the wound rot so as to ease the extractions; for wounds on other body parts, treat them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	If there is a rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupturing of the belly can be large, medium, or small; from a large wound, the intestines or intestinal cords may protrude, allowing air to enter; and suturing is more difficult, sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one, because it's harder to put the intestines back in if you don't do so carefully step by step; for this reason medium-sized wounds are better, as you can relocate the intestine to its place more easily than others. And know that there are four types of abdominal ruptures: two common procedures occur in suturing the belly wound, and the procedure for other bodily wounds is also applicable to two other specific cases, though they have some unique features too; I will describe each one and clarify them further.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine comes out, and it is a difficult thing to put back, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in tepid water only, or cook it in water with vinegar and cypress and spike, and pour this over the intestine until the swelling is reduced; and sometimes use restraining wine, which helps to reduce the inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling start to subside, moisten the intestine with water or cook mallows and let them steep, for this alleviates any blockage; and if nothing can enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is to avoid cutting it open unless there is great need; and here are the instruments to use: they slice inside along the curve and outwards, and this is their shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are exposed, put them back in place according to their natural form, if you have the ability, for it is best thus done.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is located below the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on their back, with their legs elevated above their head; if the wound is beneath the belly, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts; likewise, if the abdominal rupture occurs in one of the two halves, ensure that the injured part is positioned higher than the other; thus, you must manage as I say for large or medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply what is available to you; then have a compassionate assistant hold the wound with their hands and bring its lips together; this is the common method of suturing, where you take a needle or several, according to the width of the wound, leaving two fingers' breadth at its head, threading into it a good strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin and subcutaneous tissue simultaneously with the two points of the needle, until that part has been pierced, then bring together the two ends of the thread in fours; twist one end of double-threaded string around the needle from either side, then approximate the two edges of the wound accordingly, leaving two fingers' breadth and inserting another needle; knot the thread as you did with the first needle, continuing this process according to your need for needles until the entire wound is closed; the needles must be medium size between fine and coarse, because very fine ones cut through all tissue while those too thick cannot enter well: so they should be medium-sized; do not insert the needles too far beyond flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound prior to healing; then clip the ends of the needle threads to prevent discomfort for the patient when lying down, and place tenting or dressing over their points to hold them in place until the wound is healed; this method using needles is more suitable for small wounds, since it requires only one or two needles; the second kind of suture is common, where you approximate both edges of skin with subcutaneous tissue together onto a needle holding medium-strength thread; when you have pierced these four parts together, return the needle to the point at which you began, like sewing cloth; leave between each stitch the thickness of a little finger as space; this kind of suture is suitable for humans, and I used it on a man with a wound in his belly, sliced open by a knife, more than a palm wide, exposing intestines measuring two palms across, and located mid-abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed within fifteen days, I treated him, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	The physician had judged him to be dying, but it was a miracle; I did not treat him with ointment because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; instead, I applied old cotton twice a day on the wound and washed it with water and honey until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pierce from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced through the heart from right to left, leave the siphon or skin where the needle entered, and make it pierce from the other side, from inside to outside; the understanding of this stitch is that you sew like pelters do with furs, leaving a fold of the siphon on one side and taking it up again on the other until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, as Galen accurately describes it, is done like this: Some physicians bring the two parts together naturally and apply one head of the wound to the other, in such a way: they pass a needle through one head of the navel nearby, and make a hole only there, leaving the two heads of the navel; then turn the needle and pass it through from outside to inside, to the two heads of the navel; then pierce each part from outside to inside in two other heads of the navel that are on the opposite side. This is the method of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word and some bear witness that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having a thread; and you must pass one needle from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who stitch leather straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more difficult than for other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those for other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, unless the fire has moved it, then let the intestines dry out and heal; then apply a powder promoting flesh growth, and if the fire has moved it, apply any present ointment until the wound heals; and cauterize the sinews, and close up the orifices; then treat the wound as with the others, until it is healed; and if you don't have medicines, apply old cotton immediately after it starts to heal, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may affect the principal members, then you must wet a light linen cloth with moderately warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the armpits and under them; and if there is pain or inflammation in the bowels, which often happens, then administer a tepid wine enema, especially if the inflammation reaches the intestine; pierce it inside, and know that when it's the large intestine, it is lighter to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jejunum" cannot heal when they are torn, and this is because of the small veins that run through them, as well as their delicate nature and proximity to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the serous membrane tears away from the wound, reset it like you would with the intestine while it is fresh; but if it is old and has turned green or black, then you must bind the blackened area to prevent bleeding since veins and arteries are present there; next, cut what lies between the two ends and attach the two shoulders hanging down on either side of the wound so as to facilitate extraction when the serous membrane falls, and the wound bends.
de la routure dou boueil	Of mouth rupture.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.
