The bleeding of the veins behind the ears aids in cases of chronic catarrh and migraine; and as I told you about the qualities of bleeding, it is that you raise the patient's head, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then strap the patient's neck with a bandage so tight that two veins appear at the back of each ear in two places depending on the head: grasp them therefore with your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, make an incision there; then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift up your hand to cut all the vein above, and cut both skin and vein quite through two fingers' breadth, allowing as much blood to flow out as you wish; then draw the thread and bind it tightly so that it be healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries located in the temples is beneficial for treating long-standing migraines, persistent otalgia, and habitual lachrymation from the eyes. The quality of this procedure I will explain as follows: have the patient hold their neck tightly so that the two veins are clearly visible; feel the pulse beneath your finger, then bleed afterwards; raise your heart above the vein with your index finger, insert the lancet underneath, lift the vein upwards and incise it like you did for the other two veins; let the blood flow according to your need. Then release the patient, put your finger on the wound for an hour, apply cotton, bind the wound tightly afterwards, and leave until healed. We have previously discussed their cauterization and extraction in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is just as valuable as the bleeding from the cephalic vein for ancient diseases, and for migraine headaches, and redness [of the face]; and its qualities are such that the patient must strain their neck by twisting it, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called a "fosseur," of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the point of the instrument over the vein, and press it down with your hand or another object, allowing blood to flow out according to the desired quantity; then release the patient's neck and bind the wound so that it is tight but not too tight, and never use a wide flame for this.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame should not be too sharp, and do not bleed across the grain [of the wood], as there is bone nearby, and perhaps it might break the flame when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the two armpits helps the eyes, and for tinea, redness, swelling in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient must twist their neck with some cord, as before; then bleed them, and let the bleeding be across, a little from the length of the flame, a little wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break; then make an incision for the blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, binding it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein in the nostril is good for fever and sudden madness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that appears on the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient must twist their neck, then grip your nose with your left hand, take a subtle long flame, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open easily there, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of two guindeges aids in the treatment of neck dislocation, and at the beginning of surgery, and for many illnesses, impetigo, caries, herpes, and abscesses; and the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient must press his neck below one another as we have said; and let the masters be above the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a seat, then open the vein from end to end quite widely, then remove blood moderately or as much as necessary; then do likewise in the other wound, then untie the ligature, and press gently around the wounds so that the patient does not choke; let it be until morning when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of lips.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of veins on the upper lips aids in ulcers inside the mouth, gum corruption, chapped lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Make the patient sit in front of you and hold their neck firmly as I've explained; then turn back the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right upper lip and the other on the left, which are recognized by being black and having small dark veins around them; so cauterize each one, and if you don't know or are in doubt about which is which, simply burn the larger of the two on each side, and do likewise for the upper and lower vessels since they must be treated alike.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	The cauterization below the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins that lie beneath the tongue is beneficial after bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it treats the narrowing of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and mouth ailments; the quality of the bleeder should be such that the patient lies between your hands facing the sun, and you lift their tongue, and look under each side for a black vein: bleed both, but do not go too deep, as arteries lie beneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by incising with a wide martin flame, or with an olive-shaped subtle point like a sharp knife, and this is called "anesil"; they are broad and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame martin is very renowned, and it is broad as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the deep veins filled with thick and visible blood, and those containing thick and cloudy blood; this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and slender, and is used for bleeding delicate veins where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids in illnesses that are below the throat, and on the neck, and in the lungs, and in the stomach; and it is important for the bleeder to bleed carefully, and to beware of the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the artery, and bleeding occurs, you must stop it, as I said; and the wound should not be gripped but cut like a vein.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the basilic vein does not open clearly, you must expose it, and change to another one; or take a part of it, or treat in its place the vein in the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it like a vein, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of incision, it is better that you stretch out the arm and feel for the pulse; then mark this spot, and tie up the arm, and cut the vein like a vein; beware not to wound the artery when you see swelling, as that is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: therefore hurry and apply pressure with your finger for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, as this often happens; bind his arm, and let it be, and do not move the patient; be cautious, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not staunched and you faint, and a physician is not present, then sever the artery if it is exposed, for this will stop the blood flow from his head; staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fig bark, split it in two, and take one half and apply it firmly until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then treat him as we have said, with powders that staunch blood; and let the staunching not be grievous in many ways due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's binding.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The draining of the vein in the middle helps to draw out blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to beware of the nerve that lies beneath, and if he pierces too deeply there, and finds the nerve, and it swells and the incision is grievous, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears often, and if it does not appear in some men because of its subtlety, then you must treat it with a small instrument; and avoid the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The incision of the cephalic helps, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to incise by pricking with an olive-wood splinter or a myrtle splinter, for this is the safest of all veins, as there are neither nerves nor arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest place, and do not worry if it is wrong the first time, just start again; and perhaps some people's places swell when they make a mistake the first time, but this does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the discharge is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done for the sake of bleeding but to maintain health and avoid future illnesses; and let this bloodletting be performed in one of the three veins: namely, the cephalic, the facial, or the basilic vein; and one must bleed at the beginning of Lent while fasting, and in autumn and winter after eating when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first day or third, two to three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding administered for illnesses has no determined time, but it is done when needed, day or night, at all hours and at any time; and one should not bleed children under fourteen years of age, nor a pregnant woman within the first four months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not bleed the elderly who have passed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, regardless of the method, they should first empty their intestines with a gentle enema, if there is an excess of feces retained, so that the veins do not draw harmful waste from the intestines and affect the principal organs; one should not bleed those who are overly full from eating, or drunk, until they have sobered up, nor those suffering from dropsy; furthermore, refrain from bleeding after a bout of colic, vomiting, abdominal pain, excessive intercourse for women, fatigue, lack of sleep, fasting, and any exertion of strength or body. Then purify the humors if the blood is thick due to food, drinks, or medicines, if you have the means to do so; then take a bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin out the blood, and bleed from the vein on the inner arm below the elbow, as we mentioned earlier; guard against any exertion, pain, lust, and similar things that day; be at rest and cheerful, and ensure the bleeder is higher than the person being bled, and rub the patient's arm two or three times, then tighten the cord moderately, for if it is too tight or narrow, blood cannot flow through; then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the bleeder's flame with a little old oil, then place your left hand's finger on that vein below the bleeding site to prevent the vein from collapsing when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that escape like ropes when bleeding, and some of them are filled with windiness, so much so that when one applies the flame on it, it withdraws from the flame and cannot open the vein; thus is one in such a situation; if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, because of this, those who bleed must be mindful of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, it is good; but if not, one should try again a little lower or higher without swelling the site.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the site is swollen and the patient fears it, leave it for one or two days without binding the arm: perhaps hot abscesses will form; do not enter the bath, but start bleeding again if you wish; and if the opening is small, the blood flows out subtly and you doubt that there isn't enough blood coming out as much as you want, then apply a flame directly on this same opening; work slightly above it instead of swelling the site; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not reopen the wound, but apply a poultice of oil, for it lightens the body's blood and is soothing to this place where the oil belongs; thus administer the oil-based ointment in every dressing that you treat wounds with to staunch the flow of blood; this same action thins and disperses [the blood], when applied on the wound, if subtlely so as not to cause too much pain.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess forms there, which often happens, especially when it has not been dressed previously or the opening of the wound is small, then hasten and apply to the place a moist sponge in warm water and salt, pressing it for an hour; you must do this after the blood from the wound has drained, and if after some days a blackness or greenness remains there, it will not harm [the patient]; but if you see any redness, apply something of aloe or myrrh infused in calamint juice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	For many times abscesses and appearance occur in the healing of the basilic vein: so put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the touch of the hand, then this is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid anything that might impede circulation of the artery; instead apply a dry plaster to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Extract from each person's blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it as thick, let it flow until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and healthy, and requires bloodletting, to make a larger wound for them, with wide flames; and for the weak, do the opposite, and you should bleed them little and often, and you must bleed by cutting diagonally, not piercing; and this method of bleeding is safe from excessive blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body requires bleeding, give them bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are heated, draw out blood three or four times; and if they are of a cold complexion, feed them before the bleeding moistened bread with musky syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the bleeding after losing a great deal of blood, then it is necessary for him to drink broth and subtle fragrant syrup, and to make use of other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and bleed again, it is necessary that when he is weakened by excessive bleeding, he must bleed a little at a time, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to bleed his arm again after the first bleeding, and he has an illness that is intense, then he should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wants to bleed in another place, then he should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood within the body that is already heated and causes fever; thus a great quantity must be drawn out, and enlarge the opening until it closes on its own accord; then attend to all conditions of healing, and place your hand upon his pulse as he heals so that death does not come in lieu of natural closure, this happens many times when healers are negligent; nor should you, when wishing to release an arm, let blood a second time if the opening is already closed, press strongly upon it for fear that it might bend; rather leave it be until it heals the second time, or prick at the tip with flame so that congealed blood may exit through the vein's opening and apply a poultice of fresh herbs soaked in water, then lightly press.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to drain blood a second time, draw the blood in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arms is drained in place of the vein of the head because it is composed that way.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The method of draining is as follows: the patient immerses their hand in hot water until the nails are red; then they are bound loosely so that the vein appears clearly, and now you must draw from across it, neither too wide nor too long; and make a large opening, and drain close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot flow out, place the hand back into hot water, and let the blood run into the water until enough is drawn; but if this is done in winter, do not re-immerse the hand in hot water, for it is done more often in winter than summer; and draining from this vein is safer than all other veins, as neither artery nor nerve are harmed.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bloodletting from the vein on the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: extend the hand, immerse in hot water until the vein is swollen; if it does not swell, lacerate it; and if the bleeding occurs transversely, and you coagulate it completely, then there will be no harm. Do not go too deeply because all the nerves lie directly under the skin, which has been denuded of flesh; then immerse the hand in hot water again if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary for the patient, apply oil and lint to the vein in order to suture it; do likewise for every other wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bloodletting from the vein on the left hand is beneficial for ailments of the spleen; do everything as I have told you to do towards the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The bleeding of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all diseases that are below the body, such as uterine disorders, retention of urine, kidney disease, and similar illnesses in the hips, thighs, old legs, and so on.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of this bleeding is that the patient should immerse their foot in hot water and rub it vigorously over the vein until it disappears, then bind above the ankle joint with bandages; the vein lies at the ankle and extends upwards towards the kidneys; so bleed whichever kidney is larger or at the ankle as you see fit.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it at the foot, take care of the nerves that lie below and bleed transversely like when cutting; let the flame be small.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot exit, return the foot to water, and allow it to drain fully from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the first cut fails, begin again a little above it because the skin is salty; do not be afraid of nerves as we have said before, and proceed likewise for the other foot identically.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is found at the back of the ankle, and its incision provides relief for hip pain when blood is too hot.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	The qualities of this incision are that the patient should enter up to the bath, and pressure is applied above the ankle for four days by twisting because otherwise it does not open the vein; if it opens, proceed to cut in all ways possible, including across; it is better to be thorough than too cautious since the skin is dry, and veins can often recover from such treatments.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, take some thread from where it appears on the back of the foot, toward the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and make sure to stop the bleeding that you see, then untie the binding, and apply cotton and press [it]; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Cupping incisions
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horns, or bronze, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by drawing out blood with suction, or without [drawing out] blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without bloodletting is done in two ways: either with complete heat or without [any] heat; and cupping which involves cutting and extracting blood can be performed on fourteen places of the body, some being found entirely within the head; others are in the neck; two more are in the sides of the neck; another under the chin; there is one over each shoulder; ones over the hips; ones between the two arms; ones for both legs; and ones at both ankles. Cupping extracts only small veins which are spread throughout the flesh, without weakening [the patient], as happens with vein-cutting; it should not be administered either way--with or without heat--in any disease arising from overfullness until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to illness or for treatment purposes, we must apply cupping every hour at the beginning of the month, or towards the end, and at any time; because there are some who, when they need cupping, feel heavy-headed; and there are those who experience fullness and redness in their face, neck, and head; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have an inflamed tongue, and cough up blood; and there are also those who dream about, and witness during sleep, blood, wounds, death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially during the middle of the month, we instruct them to undergo cupping after three hours in the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with inflammation ... that reaches the eyes, and it should not be done after evacuating all over the body; this venting is in place of bleeding from the head, and those with a cold constitution should not use it, nor should those with catarrh, as it causes them great harm; for these reasons, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold illnesses in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who bleed often become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Venting in the middle of the neck serves as an alternative to bleeding from the head and the basilic vein, and it is useful for narrowing of the oesophagus, splitting of the bile duct, coughs, and fullness; it should be done carefully because if it holds too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or affect the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilations at the two ribs of the neck are useful for headaches, eye inflammation, migraines, strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth; it is located in the region where the basilica vein is cut; you must instruct the surgeon to place his hand there so that he does not press on the artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventilations below the chin are useful for mouth diseases, such as gum inflammation and similar ailments in the mouth; it is located where the two lips are cut open.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilations of the shoulders are useful for illnesses that arise from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations of the armpits are just as useful as those of the three veins of the arm because they draw blood from these large veins; instruct the surgeon not to make them too deep as the place is bare flesh and has nerves and arteries beneath it.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is placed on the buttocks is beneficial for haemorrhoids and diseases below, and it should be large and made of copper, as it needs to draw well; and perhaps, if it were thin, it would break; and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs clearly heal, as they draw blood from the entire body, and are effective for old pains in the kidneys, uterus, and bladder, and relieve swelling; they should be placed at two sophens (a unit of measurement), and two ankles, but over time they weaken the body and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the suction cup is as follows: first place it empty, then suck gently and swiftly, and put it in quickly, moving evenly, and do not stop this action until you see the area turn red and swollen, and notice the redness of the blood; then withdraw, and reapply the cups, being mindful of the condition of the body, as some have tough flesh, while others have delicate pores: one must only strike once, making broad wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very dense, one must strike a third time; and when we want to draw out thin and small quantities of blood, we are content with just one blow.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to extract a lot of blood, we should repeat the process often; and if the blood is dense, strike hard enough so that the heart is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and whose pores are narrow, that you anoint the cups with an apertif and dissolvent oil: in summer use violet oil, almond oil or squash seed oil; and in winter, cress oil, lily oil, camomile oil or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is large and cold, take almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is healed has tender flesh and large pores, it should not be oiled, but instead it should be washed after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or china root water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for one who has too much moisture, they should be raised with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those with large surplus should be raised with old wine, or sesame water, or aniseed decoction, or chamomile, or others like these; and they should not be cupped before the bath nor during it, but after the bath one or two hours later; and they must not sleep after the ventilation, and he must rise up when he is to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the patient is choleric and their blood is too sharp and inflamed; then they should take cooling things like pomegranates, endive, and lettuce in moderation, and similar foods; and eat little pork fat, mutton, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And for one with a cold constitution, give them syrup of honey and medium-aged aromatic wine, which is between old and new wine, and let them eat little, few pork fat, small birds like pigeons; and on the day they are cupped, they should drink more than eat; and sometimes give some men treacle or nutmeg beforehand or afterward to strengthen their principal limbs; and thin the blood carefully, but those who are warm must not have it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without causing injury are those placed over the liver, and on the spleen, podagra, abdomen, groin, kidneys, and hip, as these body parts cannot withstand being punctured; this is not done to cause bleeding from one member to another, but rather to draw blood away from a member, just like when we place suction cups on breasts during childbirth; in order to remove the viscosity that has built up within an organ, such as when we use suction cups on the abdomen and groin to reduce swelling of those organs; it also removes pain when there is an obstruction or stone by its attractive virtue potentially removing the obstruction or expelling the stone from its position; thus they act when placed over the liver and spleen in cases where there is retained wind, and these suction cups are administered empty so as to suck only air; sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with tepid water, such as during pleuresy-like illnesses, or in a way that we fill the cup with warm alone water, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of administering the fire cautery is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm in length, with a small hole at the center just large enough for a needle to pass through, made of brass so as not to injure the patient upon application onto the limb; and it shall have within it an iron or steel rod across its middle, to hold a lighted candle wick, and these cups shall come in various sizes depending on the disease and age of those who use them; for the cups for children are different from those for adults, and for the thin differ from those for the obese.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	One should thus apply this cup in the following manner: take some wax from a candle or use ointment, and place it within the cup at the end of the rod which is inside the cup, so that the flame does not burn the patient; then place the cup on the affected limb, ensuring your two fingers are covering the hole we mentioned earlier, such that when you wish to let out some vapor you may do so, and remove the cup; take some ointment as before and repeat this process often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass used for treating pleurisy, which is entirely hollow and has no tube or opening, it is only applied when filled with water, and placed solely on the affected limb; its shape is as follows:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are only applied to limbs where cupping glasses cannot be used due to their small size, such as lips and gums, or similar areas; also on parts of the body that lack flesh, like the heel or toes, and others alike; and regarding how they should be prepared: you must select leeches filled with clear, pure water without any dirt inside them; place these in a vessel containing fresh water for one night until they are satiated and have nothing left inside their bodies; then bleed the limb using both a lancet and cupping glass until it becomes red, afterward rub the affected area vigorously until redness appears, at which point apply the leeches; and when they become full and drop off, if this is an area where a cupping glass can be applied, do so because its effects are far better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, raise the affected area with ease, and then use cold water, it works well, and then apply pressure; if the wound bleeds too much in relation to the patient's condition, soak a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on top until the bleeding stops; and if the blood flow is excessive, apply ground vitriol, gallnuts, or similar items until it clots; you can also place half of a peeled broad bean on the wound, leaving them there until they dry out at the site, this will stanch the flow now; and if more treatment is required, take additional leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the leeches do not want to attach themselves, rub the affected area with fresh blood or prick it with a needle until blood comes out and then place them on top; as soon as they sense the blood, they will adhere; once you see that they are full, sprinkle some powder of aloe and ground sel, or ashes over them so they let go.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the setting of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that if ignorant surgeons neglect this chapter, they will never turn to any of the old books, nor read a single letter; and for this reason science is lacking in our land, for I have never found any good one; and I know nothing else except through the knowledge gained from ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and through experience, and the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained within it, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary, therefore, that we state in the prologue of this book the sum of what has been said and the chapters where the sage puts his understanding; remaining true so that those who are tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When fracture, dislocation, twisting, or rupture occurs in any part of the body, you must quickly bleed the patient on both sides if nothing else hinders it, such as bodily weakness, childhood, or old age; unless the weather is very hot or too cold; and avoid eating cold foods like salads, bird meat, and goat cheese; also abstain from drinking wine, fatty meats, and overeating of any kind that fills the veins with blood until you suspect a warm abscess or an outflow of matter in the limb, so the patient returns to his first healthy condition.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meats that produce thick nourishment, or have a viscous quality, such as wheat boiled in water, and rice, eggs, feet, calf's stomach, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For too much nourishment causes inflammation and delays healing of the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the elderly and decrepit cannot heal or fuse well according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as small children; but have no fear, place large splints above the broken bone which binds and joins the limb together, until it strengthens like it was before; do not cease your efforts, and for this reason, one must nourish them with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	As there is fracture that goes sideways, another in sharpening, like the cut of a quill to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is fracture with a wound, or fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type there is its own method and proper tool for restoration, depending on how the bone remembers its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the twist in its direction, clearly apparent from outside, sounding hollow when pressed with the hand; and where there is no twisting or resonating sound to touch, and the patient feels little pain, then it may not be a fracture but rather a twist, crack, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it by hand but apply medicines that are listed hereafter and then hold it firmly in place with bandages.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which occurs in the arm bone and involves two separated parts must be aligned immediately before any abscesses develop so as to avoid them; if an abscess does arise then you should leave it alone for a day until the abscess has healed, then reset it gently and carefully, knowing that the restoration is easier than with cases where pieces are involved. Then secure it, as outlined below
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, then extend it in two parts, whether it be arm or leg or a small limb of your own hand, or with two ligaments, or one and also your hand; place the member according to its natural shape so that when the damaged part of the limb has been separated, bring all appendages back into their places as best you can without causing further injury or pain, and align well the heads of the bones according to their proper forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the patient will feel it with their hand if you think it is not well: handle it gently, and do not hold or squeeze too tightly as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in limbs through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the limb is in place, discipline the patient well to not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, when turning or moving in any other way; and watch closely that the limb remains secure without causing any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain felt, it is not yet in place, and you must position it so that no pain is caused; be careful that it is set straight to avoid any twisting once restored; the quality of the broken limb will depend on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness, size, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For smaller limbs like arms and fingers, wrap with soft and fine linen cloths; for larger ones such as thighs and legs, use wide and sturdy bandages, for broad bands embrace the entire large limb and constrict it evenly from all sides, so that there is no strain; then bind with light padding, three or four turns depending on the limb's size, and tighten your hand a little over the whole bandage; then go above the fracture and tighten less, allowing some movement at the break; gradually loosen the band slightly until you reach a large portion of healthy tissue, then apply another bandage, rewrapping it onto the broken area; return to the part below the fracture, tightening moderately, neither too tight nor too loose as mentioned earlier; place linen pads or cloths between the bands for even distribution; bind everything above with a bandage; and finally, put your well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply soothing poultices to the abscess that are hot and reduce the swelling. Leave them like this for a few days; then bind with your splints, and let them be half of a narrow cane, cut into lengths from wood used for cleaves, or from palm ribs. Let these be shaped in such a way:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the splint that is placed on the broken bone must be a bit thicker and wider than the others; it should also be as long as necessary for the size of the limb, small or large; then bind tightly over the splints just as you did with the first binding, then tie above it with a suitable thread, like in the first bandage on the fracture. The higher up it is, the less narrow; and the thread must be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; for if the threads are too thick, as I have seen some foolish workers do their bindings with twisted linen cords, this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and there should not be less than two fingers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the tips of the ribs after being constricted in their chest, place sterile pads made from linen or wool beneath them so that they do not wound themselves further.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the heart is ruptured, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to constrict the ribs of limbs with fractures on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to apply ribs before five or seven days have passed, or more depending on the severity of the abscess and its rate of improvement; and here you will find the ancient method of using plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsion: take flour that has been kept against the mill wall, mix it with an abundance of egg, and apply this mixture - neither too runny nor too thick - using it in a manner common for many plaster applications designed to treat fractures across various contexts, especially those involving women and young children since it is not overly hot or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of making an emollient plaster to restore fracture and dislocation and sprain: take З abareis and ladani and enule and asafetida and gum arabic and mugwort, each weighing X З; myrrh and aloe, each weighing V З; alchiloa weighing VIIII З; grind all this into powder, mix it with egg white; if the complexion of the man is warm, then use this plaster, for it has a good composition, restores broken bones speedily, and suits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of making an emollient plaster for sprain: take mugwort and viscose mallow, each weighing X З; myrrh and aloe, each weighing VIIII З; acacia weighing VI З; Armenian bole weighing X З., grind well, mix it with water or egg white, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of plaster for joints and dislocated bones from their sockets, to ease the arising pain, and for wear on the bone, and breakage: take new wool, soak it in water and oil until cooked, and place it on the site.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good to soothe hot abscesses, and properly remove pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth-pea leaves, grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of broken bones and to reduce the remainder of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another type of plaster, even stronger than the first, is used when treating a severe abscess on the limb during restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of marshmallow, and flax seeds, pomegranate peel, melilot, mallow, and plantain leaves, along with violet and chamomile flowers; use equal parts of each. Grind them together, then mix them with salted water or regular water, or even wine, depending on the warmth and condition of the limb.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates says not to apply anything else but a mixture of wax and oil to the broken limb during restoration; he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	Galen agrees that to treat a broken limb one should apply dry things slightly warmed up like myrrh, aloe, and incense as we have previously mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.
