Another type of plaster that is beneficial for injuries and pain: take mugwort and chopped human hair, or feathers from a bird, and viscum, and equal amounts of flax, grind them all together, make a plaster and bind it in place.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove the binding a little while later, and take care to ensure that the patient feels no pain, and check if the bone has not moved from its place; do not remove it by hand after two days. If there is pain at the site, or itching, lack of rest or swelling, then hurry and release them, and remove the plaster now; take light cloth, and a sponge from the sea moistened, dip in water, and lift up the site until the itch ceases and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then apply dry wool, dampened with water or rose oil, and bind it carefully overnight until you are sure of warm abscesses; and bring down the inflammation of the limb, and remove all pain, then recommence gentle binding, and a little plaster but do not bind so tightly as before; gently treat until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has cooled, turned red, caused pain, and swollen are all gone, and you need an ointment and bandage, start over by applying them as before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If nothing from what we've mentioned affects the limb, do not undo the dislocation for three or four or five or seven days; sometimes it is left for twenty days, as observed, until the fracture heals and the flesh closes in on it; then restrain it more than before, and thicken its flesh, as I said previously; if you see the area drying out excessively, know that nourishment cannot reach it; therefore, warm it with lukewarm water each time you release it, every three days, and slightly loosen the restraint; through this practice, nutrition reaches the limb, and corrects what folly does to restore the limb crookedly: this is harmful, and such work is fearful, and I see nothing else but to leave it be and treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various kinds of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many types of fractures exist, with diverse forms and distinct causes. There are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the blade removes all bone down to the soft tissue beneath it, as if hacked away; this type is called 'hachure'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword chops through the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called 'absolute'; the wound from these two types of fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a fissure caused by a stone or blade, or falling onto stone, or similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that reaches the periosteum, whether it be above or below the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that penetrates the bone as subtly as hair, and the crack is small, thus this fracture is called 'capillary'; and if the wound is caused by striking stone, or by falling, or similar, and it drives a piece of bone inward, with the hairs bent like those of a cauldron maker when hammering on cauldrons; in such cases the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	It occurs more often in those with moist bones of the head, such as children; and it happens for all types of fractures that small fragments are detached like stars; I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We know all kinds of fractures by their reduction on them, examination at the site, and through the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The bone's appearance is known for when it has been exposed, and one rubs above it, then the black fracture opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the fracture, take heed of the patient's accidents and mishaps, and if you see no ill accident such as vomiting bile, loss of wit, stiffness, numbness, feverishness, eyes issuing forth fire and reddening, or other similar things in various constitutions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no frightening accident and hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture first occurs to you, and it is in winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can do this.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the flesh beneath the bone become corrupted and bring about the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture reaches up to the membrane covering the brain, you must split the affected part thusly: take hold of the head of the wounded patient and uncover over the bone in all ways possible to you, as well as on the shape of the wound gently. Should there be any discharge of blood or abscess formation upon uncovering the bone, apply this appropriate treatment method, filling the place with cloths dampened in rose oil; let the wound rest until the hot abscess has subsided and you are assured that bleeding stops; then begin to remove [the foreign body] from around the bone, doing so as follows: one method is to cut a narrow incision at the front of the site.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is that you have several different blades, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, made of iron or steel; use them lightly so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	If the bone is hard and dense, you must pierce it around rather than using blades with trepans, not too deep so that they do not penetrate beyond the skull bone, and each should have a margin or circle at its tip to prevent it from passing through; you need several of these, ensuring each fits into place according to the type of bone, thus providing trepans for all areas of the skull.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities required to drill around the broken bone are that you place the auger on the bone, and turn it with your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the auger elsewhere a little afterwards, and do this all around, then cut with the incising tools the space of the bone between the holes, and do this as finely and lightly as you can, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone by hand or with any instruments like pincers; take care not to touch the brain or the membranes.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you reshape what remains of the bone with any other instrument similar to an incising tool, but it must be more sharp and fine than the other incisors; if there are small bones or scales remaining, remove them lightly with some instruments; then clean the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, which is safer; he praised it greatly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a portion of the bone, where the fracture is visible, so that when you have uncovered that part, place beneath it the head of this lenticular chisel, which is shaped like this:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, as the blade is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edges face towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet above it, so that you lightly chip away at the bone all around, and be mindful of the membrane beneath; if it adheres to the bone, remove it carefully, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the marrow, and the bone is merely clipped from above, with small pieces present, it is necessary to remove this roughness, and scrape off the flakes with a fine rasp that you must have in various quantities, to suit each place most suitably, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use large rasps first, then finer ones, and do not cease until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-trimming and fine scraping operations, you must adapt accordingly to its location; this is something that has not been fully addressed by those who have studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is uncovered, you must take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth, doubled over twice or three times, dampen it with wine and rose oil, and lay it atop the first cloth; do this lightly so as not to burden the wound, then apply another bandage above it, but do not tighten too hard, only enough to keep the wound in place; leave it like this for one or two days until the hot abscess is alleviated, then untie it and treat with non-biting medicines such as lily roots, oat flour, incense powder, aristologist preparations, and similar things; make a powder from these and apply to the wound, then use gentle non-biting remedies; ensure that the wound remains clean, neither leaving ointment nor letting pus accumulate, for when pus accumulates on the brain's membrane it corrupts and can cause great harm to the patient; when biting substances are applied to wounds, they corrode.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if redness does not come from the medicine that has been applied, but because of its properties, then you must take some honey and three parts rose oil and glue one cloth with it, and place it on the afflicted area; then treat it in the manner of treatments appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose are broken, or just one, for there are two bones; and the lower part is cartilaginous, which does not break but may bend or twist instead, then it will heal.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger into the nostril and place the break evenly with your index finger inside and your thumb outside, until the nose regains its natural shape; do this gently, and be sure the patient does not feel pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the nose, and the two parts cannot come together, then you must place them equal to the head of a rather thick nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, make another one like it, and try to restore the first one on the same day, if you can; if not, after seven or ten days, when the abscess is healed, place a linen bandage over the head of the nose, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you place another one from the other side, if there is a fracture there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that you should wet the bandages with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems not to be good to me, but it is necessary that they are moistened in the concoction of egg white and flour powder; then leave the tent so that the bone hardens and the cartilage toughens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are put in place of tents, and if you have soft cloth around it, and the patient holds their breath, and blows through it; now do whatever you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess opens up in the nose while you are working on it, put some ointment or cotton moistened with rose oil, or a piece of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not appear there, apply a plaster outside made of flax seed flour and incense powder mixed with egg white, then place light tow on it, and do not bind the nose; and if the fracture in the nose is small, and the bone is broken into small pieces, extract them with appropriate instruments for this purpose, then clean the wound, cure what protrudes flesh, and seal it, as with plasters and suitable ointments; and if there is no internal wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, and place thin canes of lead until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	From the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured from below, and there is no external wound, and the break is only outside, not split in two, or bent inside, it can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then place your right-hand index finger and gently push the fracture inward, while adjusting it from outside with the other hand, until they are aligned.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is separated into two pieces, you must apply traction from both sides until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or they are broken, bind them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then place crushed cerote on the fractured mandible, and cover it with a double piece of cloth; put over the cloth a large well-made starched pad, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and secure it as best you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, release it on the third day, and then reset what has changed; apply an ointment over it, of flour from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame seed flour, after removing the cerote; cover the ointment with a light woolen cloth, and if the ointment hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed; often this takes three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses arise, apply what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, remove no part of the bone; carefully extract it with suitable instruments for that purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains no more, then sew the wound, if it is wide, and apply suitable dressings to it, to generate flesh until it heals.
de la forcele	Of the forearm.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forearm can fracture in several ways towards the shoulder, and this fracture occurs according to three methods: either it is broken and disjointed into two, with pieces, and this is the easiest to repair; or there is a break accompanied by a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when the break happens without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the bone is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then align the break with your hands, so that its form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor end to it.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need more assistance, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and make it thick according to your needs; extend and lift the broken bone, and press the sphere with your hand, so that you align the break as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the broken bone out due to it being in too deep, then the patient must often lie on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow under their shoulder, and have assistants push the shoulder down until the bone of the humerus is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the fracture to your hands, and if you find it fragmented, you must split above it; and pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join for any reason, you cut it with one of the knives that you have; but put them under this instrument, in order to protect the soft part:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it looks like a spoon, and is not sharp, and be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the strength required; and have two heads, as you see, with one wide and the other narrow, just like the opening of the wound you made when you pulled on the bones; and when you are sure that there is a hot abscess, sew up the wound, and if the tear is small or you suspect a hot abscess, fill the wound with lint and dressings according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess appears, wet a cloth with rose oil, hazelwood oil, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	You must bind the bone when it is damaged or bruised and place the plaster made with flour powder and egg white on it, cover it with light swabs, and place a rod under the armpit if needed; then take a very wide bandage about one palm in width, put double cloth over the swabs and plaster, then wrap it around with a thin strip of fabric three fingers wide and long enough to reach from behind you, so that the head of the strip hangs down. Place this on the fracture, and roll the bandage up towards your neck and under each armpit; tighten the bandage on each side, checking to see if the splint sits well over the break and that it doesn't shift from above the broken bone. If you see this, then check it every day, tightening when the wrap loosens. Let the patient lie on their back, placing a small pillow under their armpit at night so as to raise the shoulder; thus will lighten the fracture's pressure by aligning the shoulder, or bind his arm against his neck until any bad accident occurs for up to twenty days; then reapply plaster if you see it is needed. Bind and leave this way until they are healed; it takes about 28 days for most people but some less so.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Before it happens that the shoulder breaks or leaves its place in the middle, and is not pushed by force through touch; if you repair it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way possible for you; then apply over the place mill powder with an abundance of egg, and light dressings, and put a double cloth on top; then place a broad and thin silk fabric slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there are any gaps under the silk fill them with strands of linen dressing so that the silk sits evenly; and then tightly bind it all firmly with a large bandage so that the silk does not move from its place, and check the binding each day; and every time it loosens, tighten it again, and adjust the silk to make it even if it has moved out of place, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is healed in twenty or twenty-five days. And when these numbers are completed, you can release them, and be sure, for this is not an easy bone to displace.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone projects forward and pierces below the heart, push it up, remove it, and do as we have said for soothing an abscess in the case of a broken rib.
de la brisure dou pis	of a broken breastbone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The breastbone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks on the outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downwards and the patient feels great pain, lacks breath, coughs, and may even vomit blood; the bone ends are visible through the broken bone, which can be easily felt.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is done by having the patient lie frequently on their back, and place a cushion between their shoulders; then press the shoulders together and bring the ribs of both sides closer with your hands, delicately arranging to all sides so that the bone structure is as it should be; then apply plasters and cover them with fine salt poultices or other light material, wrap everything in cloth, and bind it securely to the broken bone, making sure it does not move; go around the back with the bandage in a circular motion, tightening suitably, and release every hour if the plaster becomes loose; if you need to loosen it due to corrosion, itching, pain or abscess, do so quickly, remove the plaster and treat whatever may have arisen; then apply new plasters and tighten until the wound is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that rib fractures only occur in the back and in the upper chest area near the neck, and they only bend because they are thin; one can feel it well during the examination of the patient.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And its restoration is that you set the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster, and hold it with a stick if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib fracture is displaced inwardly, the patient experiences great pain, pricking and wheezing sensations as the bone pierces through tissue; they also suffer from suffocation, intense coughing with copious bloody sputum production, immediate treatment is required, and older texts suggest extensive medical intervention for such cases.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to push the rupture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not cause this, for hot abscesses to come, if they have already arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has arrived, then drain it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you say to apply cups to the area, to draw it out forcefully, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cup may attract excess to the area due to its weak nature.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say to cover the area with moistened wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to equalize the pressure around it; then be cured by a treatment for pleurisy, involving meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone piercing the flesh, and there is doubt about their condition, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and one must place an instrument underneath to protect the tissue; thereafter, one should cut into the bone, extract it gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound together if it is large, and treat it with medicated plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess becomes inflamed, apply moistened bandages soaked in rose oil onto the affected area, and place it there; treat the site as needed for an abscess, and keep it constantly covered with poultices where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Regarding the broken neck...
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes fractures occur at the neck bone, and then it bends; also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, take note if their hands are soft, swollen, and numb, unable to move or extend, and when pricked with a needle, there is no sensation.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many cases, and if they experience relief when moved or prodded, know that the bone joints are safe, and the patient will recover with proper treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if something similar happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know their chances of recovery, observe if their feet are weakened, and if there is an accident involving hands, and wind or involuntary defecation on the back; and when placed on their stomach, if they have involuntary defecation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is reminded of it on his back, he cannot mount.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal; do not labor in vain in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not befall him, the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	The cure is thus: if there is hot abscess, apply oil of roses or fresh egg yolk until it is soothed; then place a drying and comforting plaster upon it, bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; let him not sleep on that part which pains him, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone has been torn asunder, one must cut above the heart; remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it be large, with a suture, then treat it with ointments that encourage flesh, until it is healed; and should the head of the bone be broken, which is called "the cow's head", let him thrust his fist from your left hand inside, and equalize it to the other hand in strength, then apply plaster and splint as needed; bind it tight, and if there are dislocated bones, do so above, remove them, and treat the wound until it is cured.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the broken bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the hip bone is broken, and it happens, there will be only a little lessening of motion at the head; and it hurts along the length, declining towards the rear, and the patient feels pain in the place, piercing pain, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above it, so that you are above the break; and know what type of fracture it is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, make sure this fracture is even, so that it has a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is along its length or it declines inwards, make the patient lie on their belly so that the restoration of this fracture appears to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it equal, apply the poultice, then place a stick of wood or horn above it, and hold the fracture firmly, so that it does not move; use support under the armpit, ensuring the joint is levelled.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess forms there, do not touch it until the hot abscess has cooled down, and then apply what we have mentioned before; return to restoring the dislocation, holding it as required, provided there is no ill event; this is the way of it.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	On the fracture of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, and if it is broken you must restore it according to one of the two methods. One is that you take a piece of wood of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two joints of the arm with two bindings, and bend them upwards, then place the patient on a seat. Then throw their broken arm onto the piece of wood until it reaches the elbow, and put in a wooden wedge underneath; then lift the weight or have the assistant stretch the limb downwards. Then bring both sides of the break together equally with your hands so that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method is to turn the patient onto their back and tie their hand to their neck; then order two assistants to hold each side of the break with their hands, while another holds below at all joints, stretching each part in its direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the rope below the fracture and above it, and extend each of the assistants to their assigned area.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, you must place one rope midway under the armpit and another towards the arm pit, beneath the fracture; likewise if it is toward the arm pit, a light strap should be placed gently such that the fracture aligns with the joint and the arm; then align the break as required, and hold it, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms, do not hold it for seven days; instead place a moist bandage made of soft cloth and rose oil until the abscess is healed; then secure it with emplastrum over the fracture, positioning the arm on the support and placing your hand on their shoulder or chest; apply the cloth and hold down on the support as well as the arm to keep it in the correct position for healing, unless something prevents you from doing so, or if the bone is moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will not move, use splints, and place on the break a splint wider and stronger than the others, with two inches of space between each one; let each splint be so large that it passes three inches over the fracture on either side; then strain upon the splints as I have said at the beginning of this chapter concerning fractures, more strongly but less distantly.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see that the splints are not seated and tight as we have said when restoring a broken limb, and doubt about infection being hot, leave it bandaged until the seventh day, as we have mentioned; then look every three days at the bandage to ensure no itching or swelling occurs where there is no drainage or nourishment can reach the member because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the addressee, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents occur, let him be unbound only after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place beneath the shoulder one cushion filled evenly with wool, and watch every hour during the day or night that the broken limb does not move nor its ligaments soften; if he is cured by the virtue of medicine, give him the food we mentioned before, in such a way that this food should be very soft at first; and when he begins to recover, let it become thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg must be reset after forty days in total; then he should be unbound and given baths and medicinal ointments to straighten his position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the fracture is bad and swollen, it takes one day or two months to heal.
de la brisure du bras	Of arm fractures
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the 'foscile', one small, attaching to the wrist, while the other is larger, situated beneath the little finger; at times only the large bone breaks or just the small bone, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bone is fractured, treatment and healing are easier; but when the large one breaks, healing is worse, more difficult than if both bones break together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it should be gently extended and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great pit, you must restrain him more firmly; extend him onto the cushion, and hold the wrist of his hand higher than the others, and his small fingers lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over themselves, and the cushion in front of them higher, so that the patient does not suffer any effort; then have the ministers stretch out their arms to the part below his hand or the ligament, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place the mirrors equally according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the broken pieces, place each one back into its position, and if there is any part that cannot be put together with the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut above and remove it as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with a broken wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take its cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration warm abscesses appear, then glue with a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft; bind the cloth above subtly, so that the warm abscesses are eased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the wax, and apply the plaster made from the mill powder with plenty of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint for the fracture be closer and slightly wider than the others; know that there should be six splints or arms in many arrangements: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; bind tighter above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less so when moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; let the cloths placed over the fracture be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the thread used for binding, be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have mentioned.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And return the member and the tendon after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident occurs in the member, as itching that comes to the member, you must spray the member with warm water until these itches are soothed; and let the member rest freely.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then resume the binding, and if the tendon is softened and the bone loose, or similar, treat it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take note that the nourishment cannot reach the member due to it being too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it like this for some days until the nourishment flows through it, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to pass for the patient, do not release them until 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If around this area, then bind their hands to their neck, and let their necks be even, guarding against movement and disturbance, and let them sleep on their back; know that this fracture is healed in 30 days or 35, perhaps 20 days, depending on the ingredients and the constitution of the person.
de la brisure de la main	On the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the knuckles there are few fractures, but rather dislocations happen many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or dislocated, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their back, and sit upright in front of them evenly; then place their hand on an extended cloth, and extend the minister's broken bones, putting them equal to each other until they are well-joined; apply a plaster and bandages if no abscesses appear, then put a splint according to the size of the place; it should be wrapped in one piece of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the front of the thigh bone, make a ring out of cloth and instruct the patient to tighten it onto their broken thigh; then take a long strip of cloth and let the heart-shaped knot be as large as the palm of your hand, and tie it tightly, just as required.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, then you must place a knot above and another below the break in the bone so that the hands are open and straight, then bind everything around the hand and fasten the binding between the two hands.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to either of our hands, be it the thumb, make it even as required and tie it with the broken bone; and if you see that a small straight knot can lift the fracture without movement, then do so; and if the fracture is in any other finger, such as the index or one of the others, then straighten it and bind it with the healthy finger next to it; or tie them all together as one, whichever works better for you, or place a knot above like on the thumb; and be careful during restoration and the treatment of hot abscesses, relieve those who come, just as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh/hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh/hip is often broken, and it can be clearly seen when it turns forward and backward; and its restoration is achieved by tying a bandage above the fracture site, and another one below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on their face, then each assistant stretches out their bandage to their respective side equally; this is done when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the hip joint, then one of the bandages should be towards the armpit, and the other bandage below the fracture site.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Also, if the fracture is close to the knee, then place the bandages around the knee, and ensure the stretching goes downwards; have the assistants hold the bone in its natural alignment with both hands, until it's levelled properly, then apply the plaster cast and bind it tight, taking care not to cause an abscess.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is hot abscess, let it cool down first before returning to your work and treatment; the binding is done in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap above the fracture with I hard bandage doubled in II or III layers, leaving the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the groin, and pass I long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread on top; then return the bandage over the leg and the thigh, then place stars above the fracture, and put a star above the bone of the leg; then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to even out the tightening, then start tying firmly III twists or IIII over the fracture; and as you go up beyond the fracture, tighten less; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you passed between the leg and the thigh, and tie III stars which are above, then return to below at the end of the thread until you reach beside the foot; and tighten so it cannot move from its place, then leave it like this for some time, so no abscess or swelling or other similar thing occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, release the dislocation and address what caused it, as we have said many times; and if there are broken pieces of bone caught in it, they must be removed if possible; and if not, then one must split the place open and extract it forcefully; and treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Sometimes the thigh is broken and fixed with pins, like in the shoulder or arm; however, despite this restoration being carried out as such, the patient does not fully recover.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in about 50 days or a little less or more, depending on the variations of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	From the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that there is little fracture in the knee joint, but it bends frequently.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is but a crack or a hole, which occurs in any wound and without a wound, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	One must restore it by putting something equal to what is round on its two sides until they are aligned as far as possible; then apply a plaster cast, and if necessary, insert a rounded rod, and secure it accordingly, then follow all the arrangements we have mentioned for other fractures, like hot abscesses and similar cases; apply appropriate treatment for each injury until healing.
de la brisure de la jambe	On fracture of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one is rightly called "thighbone", and the other is called "shin"; they both have similar fractures as in the arm, so the restoration process is equal to that of an arm, and all procedures apply here just like with the arm. If both bones are broken together, then the leg will be deformed on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bone is broken, it turns forwards.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, one feels great pain, it is easily seen; and it turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	So apply an extension and make it equal, and bind the bones equally; however, if the fracture is ugly and there are many fragments, then let your extension be less intense and lighter; adjust as per your discretion.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, and le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the broken bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, no fracture occurs, but in the bones of the foot, fractures may happen and to both toes; there is often dislocation in many different ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, have the patient place their foot on the ground, as if they are about to walk, and then put your foot on top of theirs, where the bones are raised, press them until they return to their original positions; then apply a plaster cast and bandage it securely, place underneath the belly of the foot a small plank with two handles, then secure it to the foot appropriately, wrap it with linen cloth and other materials as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the binding, for you will find the bones equalized, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any of the toes broken, restore them as we have said for fingers; then place in the broken toe a rod according to its length, and somewhat wider, then put beneath the foot that board I mentioned, and strain it properly; if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each toe a rod according to its size, wrapped in a piece of linen cloth, and secure the board underneath the foot; and let it rest upon the head of the table from outside the foot's belly, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I mentioned for other fractures as we have said; and treat each accident accordingly.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the broken bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's pelvis is broken, make her sit with an enlarged posterior, then incline her to the back part and have her held from behind; then fill the vagina, which is the nature of the patient, with cotton until it is as full as it can be; then help the woman stand up straight and gently lift her by her shoulders a little at a time until the cotton wool pops out through the vagina's opening; when this happens, the bone will return to its proper place along with the stool. When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton wool and after she has done so, replace it again. Continue like this for seven days or thereabouts: you will have healed the fracture by then. If you want a more efficient method of treatment, take a goat's bladder, tie its neck around a stick and push all of it into her vagina; then blow into the stick very hard until the bladder is inflated inside: in this way, the vagina will return to its proper place along with the fracture; after that fill it up again with cotton wool for a few days until it has healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or woman is broken, repair it as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice to them, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies to many the correct way of restoration: understand this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's windpipe and insert it into the penis; then wrap it with fine cloths around, and leave it for three days there, and it will quickly heal.
de brisure avec plaie	On la brisure qui est avec plaie, covient ouer et estrare les saiettes, s’il i adent; puis la voinne que li sanc en fuist a l’evacuacion dou malin sang, et quant tu as fet ceo, laisses l’aire par dedens faire sa cure.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.
