It is necessary for one who has a broken bone with an open wound, especially if it is large, such as the thighbone or humerus, that they be bled now, so that the bleeding we have mentioned will attest to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, secure it with copper sulfate, unless you have nothing else; then repeat the resetting of the fracture that very hour or day, provided no hot abscesses arise.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If hot abscesses do occur, delay the resetting until the ninth day, waiting for the abscess to subside, and don't touch it on the third or fourth day, as this will bring about an unfavorable outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is exposed on an open wound, it is fitting that you gently align it by hand, with minimal manipulation.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not equipped for you to make it equal with your hands, use this instrument made of iron which has VII or VIII fingers in length, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for that purpose, it is necessary for the surgeon to take III or IV according to what he needs in each fracture treatment; and let it be round and a bit thick so that it doesn't bend under compression when applied over the limb you are treating, and let it be sharp at the end and thicker from the middle onwards, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	It is called "palainche", so it's necessary that the curved head be placed on top of the protruding bone; push it down once until it returns, and make sure they are equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is delicate, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, you must cut away the top of the bone until the instrument has enough purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, cut it away with an appropriate instrument, either a chisel or a saw, whichever is at your disposal; then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone has been reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Do this in such a way that it is in its proper place, then moisten a cloth in black styptic wine, and properly apply it if it is on the bone; do not put any oily ointment or other such thing upon the wound, for it will cause suppuration and corruption; then administer stents once you have restored the bone, leave the wound uncovered, and cut away all covering around it according to the size of the wound, taking great care that the wound is not constrained by the fracture; many a time have foolish surgeons done this, bringing about the death or maiming of the patient; and be the binding more loose and gentle than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear an adverse outcome as we have mentioned, and find pain in that place, it should not be bound with splints; instead, wrap around it thick cloth, in place of splints, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when after one or two days you see pus emerge from the wound, remove what you have placed on it and apply healing ointment, such as Tetraconion ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is healed and rejoined.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be bandaged in such a way that the pus flows out easily downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many die, and it cannot heal but returns immediately, know that there are small bone fragments present, which is why you must carefully examine the wound, and remove all these troublesome pieces causing this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula develops in the same place or any other form of corruption occurs, you must treat it according to what he states in this chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the thighbone or shoulder blade, and other similar large bones, do not extract it, for many times this leads to death, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; if you cannot, just leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	scabs which form over a wound
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come across the condition of broken bones, especially when it is close to a joint, and it is an ugly sight to see the state of the limb; sometimes, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore if it is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, sarcocolla, galbanum, and similar others, so that you take any of these substances, or all together, and mix them with a styptic wine or with egg white or with isinglass; put this on at night in lint, and hold it tight, and do not remove it by hand for several days; then remove the lint and apply another one, until the swelling has gone down; or you can spread it over a well-prepared piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it reduces all swellings above the limbs; and if the swelling has already become hard like stone, and must be removed, scrape off its surface, and cut away the excess matter which appears; or remove it with a scraper until it is gone, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the member which is weak after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and afterward the limb remains weak and sensitive, it occurs due to many causes: one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and was not tied as it ought; or because there were too many bindings, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive draining; or because of great movements, not at their proper time; or because they have little blood in their body, thus remaining weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and soften their body so that blood multiplies within them; administer a bath to them, and bring joy and lightness; then place a poultice on the limb such that it draws great nourishment to it, and often wash with warm water until nourishment reaches the limb; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of a limb twisted after the injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone appears clearly, and the form of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those foolish people who say that one must break the limb anew; many fools have done this in our land; these practices are condemned, and great harm can come from them, even death. However, if the swelling and pain are fresh, then they should be treated with warm water, or softening herbs boiled together such as mallow leaves, roots, and honeysuckle flowers, and other similar things; and make a poultice of this, for instance out of daucilon well prepared, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, then apply the poultice; alternatively you can use soaked figs which have been ground together with bran, along with other medicines that soften swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by continually and thoroughly rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Be moved gently every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the stiffness is removed and hardened like stone, and it needs to be taken out with an iron tool, then you must cut carefully up to the bone, using a fine incision instrument; place a stitch and focus on the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to anyone, you must reset it immediately without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the joint swells, and it may be reset with difficulty; therefore, one must not move it while swollen: often causing spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this occurs, make the patient bleed, then leave him alone until the abscesses are soothed; then bathe the limb in hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it returns to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws become dislocated on both sides, and there are two types of dislocation: either they are slightly out of place and softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and saliva runs from the mouth which cannot be contained, nor can they close their mouth, and speech is impeded.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through various movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and full, you must reduce it quickly without delay; in such a way that the assistants hold the patient's head, and push one of their hands on the mirror under his mouth into the root of the dislocation of the jaw, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be outside to apply equal pressure; and instruct the patient to relax and move his jaws from side to side.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the assistant puts it back in place so that it returns to its position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reduce, especially if they are both jaws together, soak them in hot water and oil until you can gently reduce them; do not delay the reduction as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are returned evenly and the patient's mouth is well closed without softening it, apply moist cloths in a cerate made of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind them with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on their back, and place two cushions under their head so that it does not move to the right or left, nor should they strain themselves to chew but take light food until the pains are gone and jaws healed; then they may eat what they want gently, without straining to open their mouth for eating or drinking until the jaw is fully mended.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two jaws cannot be set back in place at once and are not restored to their proper position, fevers and swelling usually follow, along with possible diarrhea and maybe vomiting clear mucus.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is ruinous; and often the one it befalls dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	On the fork.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The collarbone cannot be dislocated from within during its course from the side and below, but it can sometimes be dislocated outwardly and this is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the treatment is as follows: have the patient lie on their back often and extend their arms; then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; next apply a plaster and bandage, and secure it; and the head near the neck cannot be dislocated; but if it is, and if it dislocates again, reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage, securing it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; likewise, the shoulder head is treated when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: thus one is that it dislocates to the side below; and the second is to the part of the back; and perhaps it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside towards the nerves; and many times it dislocates beneath towards the side, especially in those who have little flesh, because for these it dislocates quickly; for those who have enough flesh, it dislocates with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps there are some men who experience a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	The dislocation is recognized when it falls towards the armpit, creating a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, with an obvious disparity; there will be a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and beneath the armpit where you touch the head of the shoulder, like a hole; the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose or move in any way; if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden as you can clearly feel it upon touching; this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is recent, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is for the minister to lift the patient's hand upwards, then place your fists beneath the armpit, and raise the joint with force into its position; the minister lifts the hand and stretches it upward, then places it underneath; this will cause discomfort.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come about as we have said on ordinary days afterward, then the patient must be bathed in warm water; and bring them soothing and softening emollients, such as a decoction of althaea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and let this be administered; then remember to place the patient supine, and put beneath the stool a pile of woolen cloth equal [in thickness], neither too soft nor too hard, then place the patient's heel on the stack, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the affected hand; and another minister holds the head of the patient, so that it does not move downward; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish to reset it according to this manner: and have present a man who is stronger than the patient; and be directly facing the side, push their shoulder under the stool of the patient, and lift the stool upward, such that the patient hangs in mid-air; and another minister pulls the affected hand downward towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, attach something heavy to them, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one resets it in another way too: you stick a long pole into the ground, so that the shoulder is as taut as a bowstring, and it should not be too thick or slender; then place the patient on top of it but have soft cloth underneath, and let the patient rest their length along the pole; then extend their hand far to the other side in front of them, and the joint will return to its place immediately; if it does not want to go back for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a pole two arms long and four fingers wide, with a rounded end so you can easily insert it perfectly underneath the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie on top of the head with a soft cloth so the wood does not hurt the patient, then place the wood underneath the patient's armpit; extend their arm over the long piece of wood, and tie the shoulder to the wood, and the arm to the head of the bed; then put the arm across an inclined bench made from a board with width, and let the hands be extended downwards, and leave the rest of the body hanging on one side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how, you must put underneath the armpit an equal-sized wool sphere, then apply the plaster prepared with mill powder, incense and egg white all over the shoulder and around it; then wrap the strap under the armpit appropriately, and turn the ligature back onto the plaster, and embrace the hand on his neck, and let the hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And one should eat little, so that the limbs are strengthened, for he will heal faster; then eat more after five or seven days and move around; if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or any other reason, you must apply cautery to three openings, as described before in the chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and one cannot lift their arm upwards, know that the nerve at the shoulder's head is cut or stretched or weakened; know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs near the armpit, and in the chest area or behind, is caused by a pushing force, and stretching of hands, and it should be treated elsewhere; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, the limb develops cracks and moves sluggishly, let the patient bathe frequently until the cracking is relieved and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of shoulder dislocation:
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is repeatedly dislocated and returns partially; if it is dislocated from all sides, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not fully corrected because one can see and feel it; and it dislocates according to each person's anatomy.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick man's wound with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, and he cannot bend his arm or reach his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	You must reset it before abscesses form, for if an abscess forms first, the resetting will be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset at all, especially when it is at the back; this type of dislocation is worse than others, causing more severe pain, and possibly death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that you can reset it with your two hands holding his hand; stretch his arm outwards, and place your hands around his wrist according to the wound above, below, and beneath, and push the joint towards its bones or at the root of his palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is forward, it returns when he bends his hand towards his hand, and pierce with a knife from the root of the palm which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and let two people extend the arm, and the other two hold it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from side to side, then wrap a long and wide double cloth around it; when you see that the joint has met with the hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then put the joint back in place firmly until it returns; and once it is in its place, apply dry poultice on top using egg white, secure it tightly, and bend the arm onto the patient's neck, leave for a few days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, untie the bandage and leave it; but if you see that the joint does not hold well, start over with the poultice and the bandage, and let it be for a few days, until it is securely set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain and swelling after resetting the joint, and it changes, bathe and gently rub it, pressing until it is soothed; or place over the joint some fat sheep's wool, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and put him in the bath; when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then apply the wool again, and put him back in the bath; do this two or three times until it is healed; if you see any discharge, place warm moist cow manure mixed with butter on top, and bandage it up; it will return to its proper condition.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The wrist dislocated and its return is light, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be reset immediately after the dislocation, unless the place is swollen or an abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reset is done as follows: you place the injured hand on a table and have assistants extend it, and you watch to ensure its alignment so that he places his palm over the appearance of the wrist and presses until it returns. Nevertheless, one must check if it is in proper place; then the patient can place the back of their hand on a table for extension and reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place their wrist on a table and you put your hand over that appearance of the wrist.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that's good But if not, apply a strain of emollient plasters for hot abscesses, and leave it like this without re-starting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, the joint remains deformed; and this causes no harm to the patient as long as the limb is weak, and unable to grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves or arteries are severed, so there is nothing else to tighten except by cauterization near the wound, perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the limb is in place, apply the plaster we mentioned, then a strain and leave it for five days, then release it and leave as such.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any graze, then bathe it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the finger of the hand is dislocated on both sides, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then extend the finger and push the dislocation with your thumbs until it returns, then hold the head of the finger and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated; leave it for two days, and then make it equal that day; at night bind it, as we have said, and untie it during the day, and make it move, and tie it at night; do this often until it becomes narrow, and do likewise if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated on another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	For the dislocation of the spine's back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine's back or neck is dislocated, and there are multiple dislocations, there is no treatment as death quickly takes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that feces come out uncontrollably, unable to be held in, and often certain members become weaker, either both thighs or both arms or one; and often the spine curves into four parts; the one which curves backwards is called 'gilbositez': its treatment is that you straighten it if the gilbositez came from childhood: there is no cure nor total healing.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And the one which comes from falling or blows or similar things, ancient ways of treatment say there is not much benefit in all this; but I have shortened it according to my intention and designed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the curvature that affects the front foot, neither a physician nor anyone else is able to cure it; and likewise with the disease that directly attacks both sides, one cannot heal them except for those that properly affect the back side of the leg as I have said before; thus, let the patient be laid on their face on an even surface, with something under his chest so he does not hurt himself; then thrust a pole into the ground at each end, one at the head and another near to the feet, tying a cord over the buttocks of the sick person, another around the hips, knees, and ankles, and two assistants should hold these cords on either side of the patient between the poles. The stakes must be firmly fixed in place as we have said before; then let the surgeon put his palms onto the spine with force until it returns to its proper position.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board three arms long and place it under the wall, have the patient lie on their side, insert the head of the board under the wall, then put the middle of the board over the spine; have the surgeons put their feet on the other end of the board, pressing hard until it returns to its place; if you wish, do it with a machine that turns in the direction of your hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Insert two posts into the ground one arm's length apart from each other at the patient's head and another pair of posts an arm's length distance away near their feet; allow for a span between each post, both above and below, and drill a hole in each post to accommodate the winch which should be firmly anchored in place so as not to move; install on either side between these two pairs of posts one turning-post with another pair of smaller posts, one arm's length long, inserted into it for cranking; then attach the rope that runs through the eyelets to the winch at the patient’s head and another rope from the other end to the opposite winch near their feet so that each assistant turns their respective crank until the spine is aligned as we have described.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with an abundance of egg, then pack with gauze, and insert a wooden splint three inches long to prevent bowing at the site of the kyphosis and healthy vertebra; then bind with a bandage as we have said, and feed the patient nutritious food until healed; and if anything happens towards the end of healing, administer softening and soothing medicines along with the splint we mentioned earlier; sometimes a piece of lead is inserted, and at other times the swelling appears behind the last vertebra in the back, and it is thought to be dislocation; but this is bone protruding, therefore one should not presume: perhaps it would cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of dislocation is as follows: when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it appears longer and the diseased knee is more apparent than the healthy one; the patient cannot bend their knee fully to the ground, and there is swelling due to hot abscess near where the thigh bone comes out, because the head of the femur has come loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign for him to whom it comes out of place is as follows: this mishap is contrary to those mentioned previously.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs for him in whom it occurs previously are as follows: he stretches his leg according to its completion; nevertheless, he cannot bend his knee without pain, and if one wishes him to walk, he cannot do so forwardly, and he holds back his urine, and his groin swells, and when he goes to stool, he does so on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has dislocated his hip are that he cannot bend his knee or double over, and one leg is more twisted than the other; the groin area is softened, and the head of the thigh bone is located under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	We reset this type of dislocation by restoring the joint if it is old and remains in its displaced position without treatment, but we must avoid causing further damage.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	In the case of a fresh dislocation, there are four types of dislocations; you must act quickly and return the joint to its proper position by stretching it both inside and out and moving it from side to side, perhaps it will go back into place without further treatment being necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong assistant and have them grasp the leg firmly with both hands, or bind it tightly with a bandage above the knee; another assistant should place their hands under his armpits, then secure him with a soft bandage around the thigh; another holds the head of the bandage; they all stretch in an upward and downward motion simultaneously until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation is corrected, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must treat it similarly when the dislocation is within. You should have the patient lie on their healthy side, then place the bandage around the root of the thigh and below the hip joint, stretch the bandage upwards towards the hip joint, and also towards the groin; another assistant takes his arms, embracing the thick part of the affected thigh, and stretches it outward forcefully: this will restore it to its proper position now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in this manner that we have mentioned, then it is necessary for you to bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft bandage over their heels and knees; let the affected leg be extended twice as much as the other one; then hang them by the head from a wooden pole so that they are suspended above ground at around 2 arms' length. Command one assistant to embrace the top of the thigh, while another assistant is hanging with the patient who embraces the thigh strongly, for the joint returns now hastily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocation is outward, let the patient lie as we have mentioned in the case of curvature; tighten the bandage on the affected leg properly and also on their foot; then place two red-hot irons, one by the head and another at the feet, then insert an iron rod between the thighs of the patient into the joint; ensure there are moist cloths placed around it so that it does not burn the patient, then stretch each minister towards him, and let the physician hold their hand level with the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place them on a board, i.e., table, and press it as we said for hernia, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it's necessary to stretch the affected leg until the point I mentioned; place your knee against their hip, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	If the dislocation is on the outside, it's not necessary to stretch the affected leg upwards or lift it off the ground; instead, position it as if the hip were dislocated outwards, as we said about lying on both hips; let them lie on their face, and extend the tie as mentioned earlier, pressing on the joint against a board; when the patient stretches out their legs and they're even, adjust the thighs, apply an ointment and strain with a bandage so that the hip doesn't move; rest for three or four days, then remove it, reapply the plaster, and if you see that the legs are even, bind as before, and leave it on for three days; then release them again and let them walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, from within and without, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg towards their thigh, and if it does not reach their thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit straight, and stretch their leg if they can, and place your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and pull it between your two hands, then bend the two sides of the knee sharply; and another minister stretches their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they lightly touch their leg to their thigh; and apply a plaster cast over it, and make them rest with their leg on their thigh, and bind them tightly together for three or four days, then release them; and do not let the patient walk, until their limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not broken, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes fully dislocated, internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and mostly in front of the dislocated part; the reset should be done gently, and when it is only bruised one must extend it lightly by hand.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright, and have an assistant hold them by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, and twice more with your left hand, then stretch it upwards, and firmly push the foot upwards; do this two times as we have said, pulling and pushing on the foot; if it comes back into place, that is good; but if not, begin the work again, for it will come back out; and if it cannot be reduced thus, make the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and firmly fix a stick in the earth between their thighs, tying the cloth around it so as not to hurt the patient; then have an assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant stretch the foot by hand or with a cord tied above the ankle; next stretch each part equally, and let the stake be placed close beside the patient's thighs to support him when they are stretched; then place your hands evenly over the dislocation, while another assistant holds the sound leg underneath, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, apply the plaster and packing on top, binding it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, being careful that the ligaments behind the ankle are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding loosens, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and prevent the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this period is over, it is not safe that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses arise there, it is necessary that you soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	twice
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the wrist is dislocated, it should be gently stretched without effort; this is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot or back, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table, straight up, and place your foot on what protrudes from these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; when it is equalized and nothing appears out of place, put a two-legged table under the sole of their foot, then stretch it forcefully, and leave them like that for three days, then untie (the bandages); and make him rest until he heals.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound occurs with dislocation and you wish to restore it, often the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in your cure if you are not wise in this art nor have practiced it long, and if you lack compassion and mercy; nor too bold; and use cooling treatments for abscesses at first, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of health; but when there is some hope, restore the limb to its place despite the heat of the abscesses; and when the limb is back in place, administer cooling treatments again, and treat the wound as it requires with drying ointments; and should there be a break along with dislocation, bones displaced, remove them, and do what we have said for simple illnesses; and beware of falling into fear, as I've said, for your Creator will guide you according to His will, and for the safety of your soul and body.
